Second Edition 36

Current Commentary

Reflections and Commemoration of "January 28th" 37

What day is today? It is the third anniversary of "January 28th." If we recall the cruelty of the battle in Zhabei on that day, the devastation of the area, and the enormous loss of life and property, I know that anyone with blood in their veins will feel resentment and grief. However, in the three years since then, grief is still grief, and resentment is still resentment. But what has been the effect? Has the lost Northeast been recovered because of our resentment? Have the Japanese policies changed because of our resentment? Neither has happened. As for the various material and spiritual developments in our country, have they made rapid progress because of our resentment? Also, no. Therefore, resentment alone is not enough to repel the enemy externally, nor is it enough to build the country internally. If today's commemoration is still aimed at stirring up enthusiasm and only results in resentment, then this commemoration is superfluous.

Every country in the world has its own reasons for its prosperity, decline, strength, and weakness. If we ignore the reasons for its prosperity, strength, decline, and weakness, and only rely on temporary enthusiasm and fleeting emotions, then the matter will pass and be forgotten. It will not only fail to help in practice but will also hinder the overall national plan. Therefore, what the people of the country should pay the most attention to today is examining their own weaknesses and then correcting them. From our observation, the weaknesses of the people of the country can be summarized in the following ways. In addition to being easily swayed by emotions and lacking rational thinking, one is reliance. One's own strength is insufficient for self-defense. Logically, one should first start by strengthening the country, but most people still hope for external assistance. Some place their hopes on the United States, some place their hopes on the United Kingdom, and some even place their hopes on Soviet Russia. Little do they know that although the UK, the US, and Soviet Russia may have actions that displease Japan, they all have special positions and many interests at stake when it comes to dealing with Japan. They will not rashly come to help. The second is pessimism. They believe that the national situation is hopeless, so they are disappointed and commit suicide, or they become depraved and indulge in pleasure, or they cultivate personal virtue and seek personal gain. No matter how passive they are, their abandonment of themselves will not help the country. The third is shirking responsibility. The people often attribute the responsibility for the national crisis to the government, while the government, due to differing opinions, blames each other. The government, the people, and all parties should bear considerable responsibility for this national crisis. The national disaster is everyone's responsibility. If everyone can be motivated, the country will naturally become strong. And if the country becomes strong, the government will also be strong. The fourth is the lack of a national concept. In the midst of foreign invasion, every country immediately abandons the selfishness of parties and individuals to seek unity in resisting the enemy. Only China, even in the face of such a major national crisis, is not shocked to eliminate its disagreements and harmonize its spirit. It is appropriate to say that there is a lack of a national concept. The fifth is being good at discussion and fantasy. The people of the country are never inferior to others in terms of discussion and writing when it comes to handling things and planning undertakings. However, in practice, many grand plans often stop at empty words and discussions, with little further action. If this is the case, what benefit can great plans have? The sixth is that young people lack the spirit of hard work and endurance. For example, young people in Japanese universities, regardless of gender, often supplement their tuition fees by delivering newspapers and milk. They never feel ashamed of their labor. This spirit of hard work, endurance, independence, and self-respect in order to serve the country in the future has been the case for twenty years. I ask, do the young people of our country have this spirit? The seventh is the lack of discipline in the foreign actions of the people. Our country has suffered many losses of rights and humiliations because of this. We have learned many lessons but have not yet awakened. Regardless of any country, even if they are dissatisfied with the policies of the authorities, there should be a distinction between the country and the individual. Therefore, what we should advocate is maintaining a spirit of self-respect towards foreigners, getting rid of our flamboyance, adopting a polite attitude, getting rid of our arrogance and conceit. If we can strictly discipline ourselves and act according to standards, then what opportunity will others have to exploit? The eighth is that there are too many illiterate people. The strength of national consciousness is proportional to education. The Saar plebiscite had this result because all nineteen received education. Finally, it is that the Chinese people are too selfish and self-interested. The difficulty in achieving national unity and the difficulty in achieving all undertakings are all due to this. If this is not removed, then nothing can be done, let alone the great cause of saving the country.

In short, the prosperity, decline, rise, and fall of a country are not without reason. If we have points that can lead to decline and fall, then even without enemy threats, we will perish. If not, then even surrounded by strong neighbors, we can stand in the world.

Last year, the import of silver bars and silver ingots to Hong Kong was worth a total of HK$3,573,000, of which HK$1,637,000 was imported from the United States. The total value of exports was HK$9,127,000, of which HK$5,288,000 was shipped to the United States. The import of silver coins was HK$43,956,000, almost all of which was imported from China, India, and Macau. The export of silver coins was HK$34,437,000, mostly shipped to England, the United States, and China. (National News Agency dispatch on the 26th)

Lloyd George Deplores Japanese Aggression

Birmingham Former Prime Minister Lloyd George gave a speech here today, greatly supporting China, saying that he was very concerned about the situation in the Far East. The situation in that area is gradually making it impossible for the UK and the US to delay and hesitate any longer. He also said that he did not want to see Chinese territory swallowed up by wolves, resulting in Japan shrinking the country by hundreds of miles. This phenomenon must be stopped. (National News Agency dispatch on the 27th)

Only in this way can the situation in the Far East be calmed and the deterioration of the situation prevented. If the arrogant extremists in Japan always believe that there is no force that can restrain their ambitions and that they can do whatever they want, then the situation will become increasingly worse. It is a pity that London and Washington have not clearly expressed their views on the necessity of establishing a practical defense agreement between the UK, the US, and the UK, US, and Russia. Johnson only advocated that the wartime government should control the industry and that the government should manufacture military goods in peacetime, but it still cannot forcibly requisition or nationalize the country's financial resources or industry, which is enough to disperse military power and lead to defeat. (National News Agency dispatch on the 26th)

In Europe's Largest Forest 47

President Mościcki and Governor-General Pritz Hunt

Göring Arrives in Warsaw at the Invitation of Mościcki

Two Key Figures Meet in a Forest Palace for Two Days

Warsaw German Governor-General of Prussia, Göring, has arrived here at the invitation of President Mościcki. Polish Ambassador to Germany Lipski, German Forestry Director Gendel, Hunting Director Hosenfeld, and Military Attaché General Yachintler of the German Embassy in Poland also came with him. The flower car carrying Göring arrived at the central station here last night, strictly guarded by a large team of police. Because it was late at night, no one noticed. After a short stop, it drove to the East Station. After getting off the car, Göring went to the German Embassy for a rest and is scheduled to take a special train to Białowieża this afternoon with other guests. Every year, the Polish president hunts in the forest in that area, which has an area of 2,500 square kilometers and is considered the largest forest in Europe. The hunting ground is in its center, covering an area of 5,000 hectares. The last of Europe's rare bison live here, and there are also many lynxes and large wild boars. Emperor Alexander of Russia had a palace built in the forest, but he never came to live there during his reign. Now, President Mościcki will host two groups of guests in the palace. Göring is included in the second group, and his hunting days are set for the 28th and 29th. (Havas dispatch on the 27th)

Anniversary of German-Polish Compromise 48

Warsaw. The German-Polish Non-Aggression Pact was signed on January 26, 1934. Today marks its first anniversary. The semi-official Iskra News Agency published an article commenting that the German-Polish Non-Aggression Pact neither harms others nor opposes any other country. Since its signing, the good neighborly relations between Germany and Poland have been developing day by day. Whether this kind of good neighborly relation can last for a long time to create long-term stability will be indicated by future history. In short, the bilateral treaty is an excellent international political tool, more effective than various conventions and general and vague international guarantees. However, the "Daily News" said that German Propaganda Minister Goebbels came to Poland before, and there is also talk that Prussian Premier Göring will come to Poland, which shows that the improvement of German-Polish relations is valued more by Germany than by Poland, because the deterioration of relations between the two countries was originally the fault of Germany. (Havas dispatch on the 26th)

In addition, more important issues will be temporarily suspended and useful discussions can only be made after Germany expresses its attitude. (Havas dispatch on the 27th)

Inside German Politics 50

(National News Agency German Correspondent) I have lived in Germany for many years and am quite familiar with the situation in German political circles. Now I will briefly describe the measures of the new German government.

Hitler's victory over his political enemies has various aspects in Germany. If we make a comprehensive study of these situations, we can know that it is actually due to the transformation of the times, that is, the times themselves have matured. Since the Great War, German citizens have been governed by people around the age of fifty, and these people have repeatedly used the same political system in the same era.

If we study it, we can know that the administrative and economic policies of the various parties in the past reveal that the highest goal of the political figures at that time was to attack and destroy each other. Ebert, Eisberkel, Brou, Stresemann, Rathenau, and Luther all belonged to the political figures who participated in the political struggle of that era.

After this era, which lasted for twenty-five to forty-five years, the political system has not changed slightly. With the blood and sweat of Germany, war reparations were paid. No one could truly show their political talent in Germany. These political figures were only intent on being brave in political struggle, which led to cutting off their own way out, creating their own troubles, and creating their own troubles. After Bruning first formed the "Vanguard Cabinet," Hitler's voice began to become increasingly prominent. Therefore, all countries have a new perspective on Germany. At this point, those political figures who specialized in digging trenches for self-defense were forced to abandon their political desire to rule.

Today's leaders of the new German government are young and strong, twenty to thirty years younger than the government figures of the past. If we look at it from the perspective of age alone, we can know that the National Socialist political and cosmic ideal is completely different from the governments of various countries. The distinction is obvious. Only Italy's progress is similar to the situation in Germany. The vanguard of this era can make the country strong. France does not have it, and even the UK is far behind.

Today's Germany repeatedly proclaims its will for peace to the world. Today's German government is dedicated to peace in the midst of repeatedly calling for peace, because the German people themselves deeply feel the harm and benefit of war. Therefore, our call for peace is indeed the most true and just proof. Germany's bell of peace can only be heard by those who are dedicated to the scope of peaceful public undertakings. This bell is issued by the new German Third Reich in the midst of heavy diplomatic difficulties, with the psychological factor of liberating the European situation. Germany not only wishes to see France or the United Kingdom in peace, but also all the people of various countries who share this goal are happy to be friendly with it.

Airplane Torn Apart, Losing Gold Bars

(London) England and Ireland continue to be battered by gales today. Many trees have been uprooted, and numerous utility poles have been snapped. British Columbia in Canada is also suffering from wind and snow, with fourteen deaths reported. The Fraser River has overflowed, leaving thousands homeless and drowning hundreds of cattle. This afternoon in Britain, strong winds, accompanied by snowflakes and hailstones, reached speeds of eighty-six miles per hour. According to the elderly, this is unprecedented. The damage inland is significant. Heavy snow fell in London and the northern and eastern districts today, blocking many roads. This evening, a gale struck Ilfracombe, Devon, with winds reaching ninety miles per hour, toppling houses and destroying many fishing boats, but there have been no reports of loss of life. Heroic acts of rescue have been reported during the storm. A doctor and a nurse braved the storm and traveled ten miles by boat to rescue an injured person on the Shetland Islands. (Reuters, 26th)

Chahar Eastern Incident 67

Informal Talks Between China and Japan

Chinese Representatives: Zhu Shiqin and Yue Kaixian

Japanese Representatives: Matsui and Takahashi Tan

Beijing Communication: In the Chahar Eastern area, from 2:00 p.m. on the 24th (previous) to 6:00 p.m. on the 26th (present), the situation at the front line has been peaceful and uneventful. However, Japanese troops near Xifengkou near Dushikou and Datanzhen near Guyuan have been very busy increasing their deployments in recent days. According to a telephone call from Zhangjiakou, it has been determined that the Japanese troops in these two locations have increased by more than 1,600 men, and the number of armored vehicles has also increased to more than 70. In the Rehe-Western Dagakouzhen area, in addition to the Japanese army gathering more than 8,000 men and attaching a squadron of aircraft (nine aircraft), about 3,000 puppet troops under Zhang Haipeng, led by puppet Brigade Commander Wang Yongqing, are also deployed in Datanzhen and other places. Assessing the situation, the Japanese intentions towards Dushikou and Guyuan do not seem to have eased. Regarding the statement that the issue will be resolved through diplomatic means, although it has been widely broadcast today (26th), judging from the busy increase in Japanese troop deployments at the front line, whether a peaceful resolution can be achieved depends on whether the Japanese side has sincerity. Matsui, the Japanese Kwantung Army military liaison officer stationed in Zhangjiakou who came to Beiping to negotiate peace, arrived in Beiping from Zhangjiakou at 9:30 a.m. today (26th). He told people at the station that the incident could be resolved peacefully. The Japanese attitude towards this matter is to determine the "Manchu" border with China. At this point, someone handed a map to Matsui for review and asked about the Rehe-Chahar provincial border, which was clearly marked. What is the basis for the Japanese claim that the Chahar Eastern areas belong to Rehe? Matsui replied that current maps cannot be compared with old maps. Don't you know about the "Manchurian Incident"? You are not up-to-date, and I suppose you have not seen the new maps. His words were extremely arrogant. When Matsui discussed the peaceful resolution, he stated that the Japanese side hoped that China would send representatives to Datanzhen for consultation. As for what will be discussed at the meeting, he said that since he is not directly responsible, it is difficult to predict. After getting off the train, Matsui went to the Japanese embassy to meet with Takahashi Tan. Around 10:00 a.m., Zhu Shiqin, a standing committee member of the War Zone Clearing Committee, and Yue Kaixian, the Special Foreign Affairs Commissioner of Chahar Province, went to the Japanese embassy to meet with Matsui. Takahashi Tan was also present. The meeting ended at 12:00 p.m. Matsui left Beiping at 1:15 p.m. to go to Tianjin to meet with Mezu Yoshijiro, commander of the Japanese North China Garrison Army, and Chief of Staff Sakai, to report on the situation. He is scheduled to return to Zhangjiakou via Beiping next Thursday. It is reported that the Chinese side can generally send representatives to attend the peace talks. However, the selection of representatives is still under consideration, and there is a need to continue to negotiate with the Japanese side on the location of the meeting, as it should be in a convenient location. According to sources, during the informal talks between the Chinese and Japanese representatives this morning (26th), the Japanese side put forward two points: (1) The meeting location can be selected from Datanzhen, Gubeikou, and Chengde; (2) The Chinese side has not yet made any indication regarding the representatives attending the meeting. Chahar Chairman Song Zheyuan and Committee Member Xiao Zhenying went to Jurentang this afternoon to meet with He Yingqin to report on the situation at the front line and listen to Zhu Shiqin and Yue Kaixian's report on their meeting with Takahashi and Matsui. Although there was some discussion on the spot, no specific decision was made because everything needed to be reported to the Central Government for instructions. The national army at the front line is determined to deal with the situation with patience. Unless the Japanese army engages in further oppression before the two sides officially negotiate a solution, the situation should not escalate, and a peaceful resolution is hoped for. The various foreign embassies in this country are paying close attention to the future of the incident and are inquiring about the truth from our relevant parties. According to well-informed sources, the formal talks between the two sides are scheduled to take place at the end of this month, but it is difficult to say for sure until the facts are materialized. (26th)

Nanchang Headquarters Closes 68

Bandit Suppression and Aftermath Handled by Pacification Headquarters

Nanchang Communication: On January 29, 1933, Chairman Chiang came to Jiangxi from Nanjing to supervise the bandit suppression and established the Nanchang Headquarters of the Military Affairs Committee, commanding the armies of the five provinces of Jiangxi, Guangdong, Guangxi, Fujian, and Hunan to encircle and suppress Zhu Mao. After the start of the suppression, eastern Jiangxi and the interior areas were gradually recovered. However, there was the Shi Sun Incident in the northwest and the Chen Li uprising in Fujian. However, because the Red bandits could not be relaxed for a moment, the military affairs of the above areas were also under the control and dispatch of the Nanchang Headquarters. Suppressing bandits and rebellion were carried out simultaneously. For a time, the Nanchang Headquarters was the center of national military affairs and the general hub for restoring order. Chiang believed that the occurrence of bandit disasters and the recurrence of internal strife were mostly due to poor politics in the long run. Therefore, in accordance with the instructions of the Central Government to grant full power to handle military affairs in the military area, in addition to using military means to treat the symptoms, he also vigorously implemented political improvements to treat the root causes. Therefore, the Second Department of the Headquarters carried out major reforms in the politics of Henan, Hubei, Anhui, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Fujian, Jiangxi, Hunan, Shaanxi, and Gansu provinces, especially with Jiangxi as the center for refreshing internal affairs. Therefore, for three years, Nanchang was not only a military center, but also the focus of national political attention. Since Chiang launched the New Life Movement in Nanchang last February, it has swept the country. The military, political, and new movements led by Chiang in Jiangxi have all made a distinction in an era of China's rejuvenation. In November last year, the bandit nest in southern Jiangxi and the Soviet areas of the puppet central government were razed to the ground. Only a few remnants of the bandits fled into Hunan and Guizhou. The bandit suppression military operations in Jiangxi Province were completely over. When Chiang entered Nanjing to participate in the Fifth Plenary Session of the Kuomintang, the Nanchang Headquarters prepared to close down due to the lack of military needs. However, the political part was related to the aftermath of the bandit areas and the revitalization of the ten provinces. At that time, it was impossible to abandon the project halfway. Therefore, it was postponed until January this year before it was stopped. According to official news, the Nanchang Headquarters will be abolished at the end of the month. The staff members will, except for most of them who will follow the staff to Sichuan, some will return to the Third Department of the Military Affairs Committee, and another part will be transferred to the Jiangxi Provincial Pacification Headquarters to work. The rest will be given a month's salary and dismissed. The task of completing the uncompleted bandit suppression and aftermath will be assigned to the various pacification headquarters. At the time of the closing of the Nanchang Headquarters, a brief overview of military and political affairs is given to provide a retrospect.

In 1933 and 1934, Chairman Chiang was completely in Jiangxi, except for a trip to Fujian. He frequently traveled to Fuzhou, Nancheng, and Mount Lu. In terms of military affairs, in addition to quelling the rebellion in Fujian and the Shi Sun rebellion, continuing to complete the joint suppression by the three provinces, and directing the bandit suppression operations in Sichuan, more than 40 counties were recovered in Jiangxi, and more than 30 counties were recovered in Fujian. At their peak, the Zhu Mao Peng Lin Fang (Zhimin) Xiao (Ke) Luo (Binghui) factions had no less than 100,000 guns and 300,000 men. Only 30,000 to 40,000 guns entered Sichuan, Hunan, and Guizhou. In terms of political affairs, in addition to completely reforming the bandit areas, for the ten provinces, in terms of civil administration, the Baojia system was vigorously implemented, household registration was checked, compulsory labor was universally compiled, and conscription was implemented. In terms of construction, a general mobilization was carried out to build roads to facilitate transportation, and forests were planted to prevent floods and droughts. Finance was uniformly collected and disbursed, and education vigorously implemented education that combined production, upbringing, and hygiene. The judiciary cleared accumulated cases and did its best to provide convenience to the people. In addition, the provincial government worked together, the county government expanded its organization, and administrative commissioners were added to change to a three-level political system. The ten provinces were strictly ordered to complete the four major political tasks of checking household registration, clearing land and repairing dams, building roads, compiling Baojia, and completing self-defense during the training period in 1935, which were major reforms in our country's politics. (January 24)

New Tenth Division 69

Recovers Eastern Fujian Bandit Areas

Captures Many Bandits

Remnants Flee Towards Shouning

Fuzhou Communication: Xiao Gan, commander of the newly compiled Tenth Division stationed in eastern Fujian, recently took a ship from Fuding to Xiapu to supervise the suppression of the remaining bandits. The boiler exploded en route, and Xiao drowned. Xiao's coffin has been transported to Fuzhou from Sandu on the 25th. Many staff members of the Security Department went to Taijiang Wharf to greet it. The provincial government sent a military band to send it to Xilin Temple outside the West Gate. On the 26th, the coffin was re-changed and encoffined, and a meeting will be held at a later date to mourn him. The provincial government has appointed Secretary-General Gao Dengting and Security Department Chief of Staff She Nianci as funeral committee members and requested central government condolences.

After Xiao's death, Shi Honglie, deputy commander of the Eighty-seventh Division, was appointed as the acting commander of the New Tenth Division. His troops still follow the original bandit suppression plan, dividing the entire division into twenty-three detachments, which were dispatched from the Shekou Saiqi line in Fu'an County to carry out a major sweep of the bandit areas. In the past three days, they have fought fiercely with various bandits and captured many of them. According to a telegram report from the division to the province yesterday, a total of more than 100 long and short guns, more than 6,000 rounds of ammunition, more than 10 loads of propaganda materials, more than 20 loads of grain guns and machines, several loads of ammunition raw materials and steel, dozens of loads of ploughing fodder, hundreds of counterfeit coins, and a pile of banners and seals were seized. More than 30 fake government offices, fake team headquarters, military hospitals, and cooperative agencies were destroyed, and more than 100 hostages were rescued. More than 200 wounded and sick bandits were captured. The so-called strongest bandit area in eastern Fujian, with a width of more than 200 li and more than 100 large and small villages, was completely recovered. The remaining bandits fled towards Shouning. The names of the people in the bandit group were learned from the seized documents, such as Feng Pintai, the fake commander of the Fujian-East Independent Division of the Chinese Workers' and Peasants' Red Army; Ye Qi, the fake political commissar; Hu Shiru, the fake commander of the First Regiment; Commissar Cai; You Shou, the commander of the Second Regiment; Zhu Desheng, the commissar; Wei Geng, the commander of the Third Regiment; Yang Yingshan, the commissar; Wu Debiao, the commander of the Fourth Regiment; and Huang Lishu, the commissar. The names of the commanders and political commissars of the two independent regiments are unknown. In addition, each of the seven counties of Ningde, Fu'an, Shouning, Fuding, Xiapu, Luoyuan, and Lianjiang has a fake government, each with an independent battalion, with hundreds of people in each battalion and dozens of guns. Each district has a guerrilla team, with a total of 76 teams, with dozens of people and a dozen guns in each team. The fake independent division has a total of four regiments, each with four companies and another special company. The fake division has a total of more than 700 bandits and soldiers, more than 500 rifles, two heavy machine guns, one mortar, one hundred light automatic guns, more than 20 hand-held submachine guns, 140 Mauser pistols (that is, box guns) (7 or 8 Mauser pistols in each of the seven squads of the special team), 40 pistols, an average of 40 rounds of ammunition per gun, and one hand grenade per two people. According to the records in the bandit documents, these guns and ammunition were all purchased from Gutian, Changle, and Putian. Even more strangely, the bandit records show that 6,000 rounds of ammunition were received from Fu'an County. The authorities have now ordered reconnaissance and strict prevention, and are implementing river blockades in each county. The method is to set up card checkpoints in Ningde, Fu'an, Fuding, Xiapu, and Shouning to stop ships. Each county will set up a ship inspection station and, together with the garrison troops in each area, conduct strict inspections and issue inspection certificates, filling in the starting point. If the ship exceeds the starting point, it should be subject to the same inspection again, in order to be thorough and avoid theft. This matter is hosted by the county magistrates. Recently, it has been decided to issue good citizen certificates, self-renewal certificates, and residence permits to distinguish between good and bad, and to facilitate the progress of rural clearing matters. The county governments have fully prepared for this. To enrich the countryside and prosper the locality, people living outside and refugees in various townships will be ordered to return to their hometowns. Those who fail to do so within the deadline will have their property confiscated as appropriate, and implementation measures are being drafted. (January 26)

Yellow River Conservancy Commission 71

To Train River Patrol Teams

Initially Forming Three Teams of Thirty Members Each

Kaifeng Correspondence: The Yellow River Water Conservancy Commission believes that due to the constant changes in the river defenses in the lower reaches of the Yellow River, it is necessary to organize river patrol teams to assist in inspecting work sections, assisting with flood control, and facilitating construction. It is reported that the commission has already begun organizing these river patrol teams, planning to initially establish three teams, each with one captain and thirty members. All team members, in addition to some selected from river soldiers with rich engineering experience and the ability to endure hardship from the Henan, Hebei, and Shandong Provincial River Affairs Bureaus, will be recruited from among one or two people recommended by each county along the river at the request of the commission to the Henan, Hebei, and Shandong provincial governments. These recruits will be trained and then appointed. The qualifications for the team members recommended by the counties are as follows: 1. Must be graduates of senior elementary school or complete elementary school; 2. Must be between 18 and 40 years old; 3. Must be physically healthy and free from bad habits; 4. Must be of a docile nature, able to endure hardship, and suitable for rural fieldwork. When the river patrol teams encounter changes in water conditions or engineering situations during their patrols, they should report them to the commission at any time. In addition, they should pay attention to the following matters: 1. Changes in the river's course; 2. The condition of engineering projects; 3. The extent of damage to embankments and dams; 4. Rat burrows, infiltration points, and gullies; 5. The types, quantities, and locations of materials stored along the river; 6. Assisting in emergency rescue in various provinces; 7. Assisting in protecting power lines, highways, forests, buildings, and other objects in the flooded areas; 8. Cracking down on acts that damage embankments and other actions that hinder river defenses. It is also reported that after the team members are selected from various locations, they are scheduled to be concentrated at the Yellow River Water Conservancy Commission in Kaifeng before March 1st to be inspected and begin training. (25th)

Page 9

Japan's Oil Problem (Tokyo Correspondence) 72

Lack of Resources Makes Self-Sufficiency Difficult

As Japanese capitalism develops upward, exports actively increase. For example, the export of cotton cloth has exceeded that of the United Kingdom by more than 500 million square yards in the past year. Japan is both extensively developing new markets and expanding considerably in the old markets of the United Kingdom. Consequently, industrial production capacity has suddenly expanded, and Japan has become a newly emerging capitalist country. However, relying solely on peaceful economic development faces many obstacles, so military force must be used as a backing, and military preparations must be vigorously expanded.

However, in military expansion, in addition to coal and iron needing to be self-sufficient, liquid fuel, i.e., petroleum, is even more important. The amount of petroleum produced domestically in Japan, even including Hokkaido, Taiwan, and the oil mines leased from the Soviet Union in the northern part of Sakhalin Island, is decreasing year by year. In 1929, the petroleum produced in the above areas still accounted for 14.2% of Japan's total consumption, but by 1933, it had dropped to 7.8%. The statistics for last year have not yet been confirmed, but based on the general situation, it is indeed decreasing further. Therefore, can the army, navy, and the private industrial sector not regard this as a major problem at a time when a large amount of petroleum is needed?

Two or three years ago, Japan made its greatest effort to negotiate with the authorities of the Dutch East Indies in an attempt to obtain oil exploitation rights there to supplement the domestic production shortfall. However, the negotiations were unsuccessful because the Anglo-Dutch petroleum company was unwilling to easily relinquish its rights, and the Netherlands was also very cautious and unwilling to allow foreign capital to enter and exit casually. Currently, the only relatively promising area is the oil field on Sakhalin Island. However, due to the cold climate in this area, there are various inconveniences in exploitation, and transportation in winter is especially difficult. Active development is very troublesome. Furthermore, the Soviet Union is using its national controlled economic power to engage in oil mine development. Although the deposits in the Soviet mine areas are much more abundant than those in the areas leased by Japan, they can never be transferred. Therefore, Japan's ideas about the oil mines there are still not fully assured.

Moreover, the Soviet Union has recently expanded its Second Five-Year Plan, the BAM Railway, which will be completed in two or three years. The terminal of this railway is Nikolayevsk-on-Amur, across from Sakhalin Island. It already has the convenience of transportation. In peacetime, Japan's "North Sakhalin Oil Company" is definitely not a match for Soviet operations. Moreover, under the red legal regulations, Japan's private industry must be subject to restrictions on labor treatment and capital utilization. It is naturally more difficult to compete with red oil development. If military action occurs, it will feel even less secure. Japan's efforts to develop petroleum are primarily aimed at military use, especially wartime use, so it is particularly worried.

According to the current international situation, an accident is unlikely to occur immediately between Japan and the Soviet Union, but a future conflict is probably unavoidable. Then it will probably be very difficult for Japan to cross the Sea of Okhotsk and control the oil mines on Sakhalin Island. The past event of the Siberian Intervention in 1919 shows that Japan once occupied Sakhalin Island with military force. In the end, it was still unable to control it. When Russia was exhausted, it was still like this. Now that it has the power to defend itself, it is probably even more difficult to deal with.

Therefore, Japan has no choice but to make every effort to prepare alternative fuels, such as charcoal, alcohol, and the distillation of oil shale. After a long period of research, an oil shale plant was established in Fushun. However, this type of manufacturing has relatively high production costs, and the quantity produced is not very large. It is very uneconomical at present. It is reported that Japanese petroleum companies have recently been importing crude oil produced in the United States and Anglo-Dutch countries for self-refining. This method is very economical in peacetime. However, in wartime, both the United States and the United Kingdom, especially the crude oil from California, which has the largest import volume, will inevitably be cut off, and fuel will still be a major problem. Therefore, the Petroleum Industry Law promulgated in July 1934 requires that companies in the industry maintain an oil reserve of more than six months. This raises issues with the capital and equipment of the companies. Even if they can store the required amount, the need increases year by year, which is also a long-term troublesome matter. (January 17th)

Gansu Province 73

Abolishing Appropriations and Exorbitant Taxes

Annual Revenue Reduced by Approximately 380,000 Yuan

Finance Director Zhu Jingzhou Sends Personnel to Investigate Again

Lanzhou Correspondence: Gansu, located in a remote border area, has always been known for its poverty and was a province that received subsidies during the late Qing Dynasty. After the establishment of the Republic of China, the subsidies were cut off, and for military and administrative expenses, appropriations became the only way to cope. Regardless of whether the counties had funds, they were assessed each month and appropriated accordingly. Once an assessment was made, it was apportioned to the people, which burdened officials and distressed the people. Since Zhu Jingzhou took charge of finance, he had long planned to eliminate this practice, but the Ningxia war prevented him from realizing it. Until recently, with military and administrative expenses slightly reduced compared to before, he presented a request to the provincial government last year to abolish all appropriations in the counties of Longdong, Longnan, and the former Lan Mountain Circuit, starting from January of the 24th year of the Republic, to alleviate the people's hardship. It is said that the counties in Hexi are still under overall planning. Exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous levies are even worse policies. Therefore, Zhu eliminated 57 types that were excessively disruptive and detrimental to the livelihood of ordinary people, which collected approximately 380,000 yuan annually, and those listed in the first phase were also determined to be abolished starting from January 1, 24th year of the Republic. Although the public sector may suffer a slight loss, the people of the entire province will greatly benefit. It is now reported that Zhu has sent personnel to investigate by region, and if there are any similar exorbitant taxes or miscellaneous levies that are inconvenient to the people's livelihood after a detailed report, they will all be eliminated in order. The following is a list of the exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous levies that Gansu Province has implemented to abolish starting from the 24th year of the Republic.

Henan Finance Department Formulates 74

Financial Consolidation Measures

Estimated Deficit of Approximately One Million Yuan This Year

Kaifeng Correspondence: Finance Director Yin Renxian, in order to consolidate the province's finances, has formulated consolidation measures, which have been submitted to the provincial government and notified to various agencies. The original report stated that according to the budget, the province's finances could be offset, but in recent years, although politics has become stable, finances have not yet been brought into line, and the budget has lost its effectiveness. For example, the contingency fund was originally set at over 330,000 yuan, intended to meet urgent needs within a year. However, within four months of the start of the year, it has been completely exhausted, and temporary funds continue to come in endlessly. Therefore, since Renxian took office, only two months ago, temporary expenditures of approximately 300,000 yuan, which were not included in the budget, have been approved. Together with the road construction costs in southern Henan, an additional 1,360,000 yuan needs to be raised, totaling approximately 1,663,000 yuan in expenditures approved outside the budget. Among them, 884,000 yuan have been made up through various savings by Renxian, but the remaining 777,800 yuan are still outstanding and have no source. Furthermore, revenue is expected to decrease by approximately 210,000 yuan, while expenditures have increased by 770,000 yuan, resulting in an estimated deficit of approximately one million yuan. Therefore, the following four measures are proposed: 1. Maintain the budget. The budget is the standard for administrative facilities and must be maintained jointly to be effective. In the future, any funds not included in the budget will not be paid; 2. If there are urgent and unavoidable projects, they cannot be stopped due to lack of funds. However, the department must first raise the funds and approve them after the funds are secured; 3. Savings from various agencies are mostly used for self-funded expenses and are not willing to be deposited. In the future, any requests for expenses from savings will not be approved, and they will be required to deposit the full amount to meet urgent needs; 4. The revenue and expenditure of various public institutions will also be required to be deposited, and the necessary expenses will be re-issued by the provincial treasury. (23rd)

Yuehan Railway Zhushao Section 75

Two Sections of Construction Completed

A Small Section of Luojiadu to be Completed by the End of March

Yuehan Railway Can Be Reached in Three Days After Opening to Jinjiling

Guangzhou Correspondence: After the completion and opening of the Shaole section of the Yuehan Railway Zhushao section, construction north of Lechang is also proceeding actively. The section from Lechang to Chumen, with a length of 23 kilometers, has been completed and began selling tickets on the 18th of this month. Passengers and goods are temporarily transported by engineering vehicles. The Luojiadu section is scheduled to open to traffic on February 15th, and the Jinjiling section is expected to open to traffic in April. According to the engineering report of the Zhushao Engineering Bureau, the second section and the third section were connected, and construction began in April of the 23rd year of the Republic. Among them, a small section from Luojiadu to Jinjiling, with a length of about 60 kilometers, is expected to be completed by the end of March of the 24th year of the Republic. Starting from April of the 24th year of the Republic, it can be connected to the second section for traffic. Currently, the Hunan Provincial Highway has been opened from Changsha to Hengzhou, and from Hengzhou to Pingshi in Guangdong Province. The Guangdong Provincial Construction Department is accelerating the expansion, striving to connect with the Jinjiling Railway in April of this year. At that time, those traveling from Guangdong to Hankou can take the Yuehan Railway train from Guangzhou to Jinjiling, transfer to a public bus to Changsha in Hunan, and then transfer to the Xiang-E section of the Yuehan Railway to reach Hankou directly, which will only take three days. At the same time, the joint operation of the Zhushao Railway and the Hunan Provincial Highway will make freight and travel more convenient. As for the tunnel construction on the section from Lechang to Luojiadu, there are as many as 34 tunnels, with a total length of more than 7,000 feet. After sending a team to re-measure, avoiding the difficult, the route runs along the east bank of the Wu River to avoid the complicated tunnel construction, focusing on the construction of retaining walls. The original survey location was deeper, transportation was inconvenient, excavation was difficult, and the supply of materials was particularly difficult. The re-surveyed line only requires eight tunnels, and after construction began, after observing the local conditions, three more tunnels were removed, so the final decision is to have only five tunnels, namely Dazi Water Tunnel, Qimen Tunnel, Meimen Tunnel, Xinqin Tunnel, and Yuanluojiao Tunnel.

Shanghai Relief Association 76

Sending Personnel to Anhui to Distribute Relief

Initial Allocation of 150,000 Yuan for Relief Funds

A Total of Twenty Heavily Affected Counties

Wuhu Correspondence: Anhui Province has suffered severely from drought and banditry, and the disaster victims are displaced on the roads. In this cold winter, the sound of hunger and cold can be heard everywhere. The Anhui Disaster Relief Association, due to the provincial government's lack of funds, is heartbroken by what they see. The relief grain that was previously relied upon for urgent relief has now been ordered to be suspended. In addition to using the 100,000 dan that has been collected and stored to urgently relieve the most severely affected counties, it was agreed with the Shanghai Relief Association for the Relief of Drought Disasters in Various Provinces to send investigator, Chief Master Hong San, etc., to urgently distribute the relief funds in advance. The dispatched investigators are departing for the northern and southern counties of Anhui. The first batch of 13 counties in southern Anhui includes Shen Nianci, the head of the investigation team from Dongliu to Zhide, Peng Guangguang from Shitai to Qingyang, Fang Weilan from Shexian to Xiuning, Zhang Zigan from Huo County, Qimen is undecided, Chen Moyan from Jixi, Xu Yuntao from Ningguo, and Jingde, Jixi, and Taiping, because they have suffered the most from bandit disasters, are designated as special zones, with Zhu Jiatian as the chief executive and the executive director of Jingde, Xie Ji'an as the executive director of Jing County, and Jiang Xuwu as the executive director of Taiping. The seven counties in northern Anhui include Wang Choutian from Qianshan, Zhang Qiaofu from Taihu, Zhang Ziyang from Lihuang and Huoqiu, Heng Yongquan from Huoshan, and Huaining (i.e., Anqing). Tongcheng are currently undecided. Zhu Jiatian and Xie Ji'an, etc., have departed today to go to Wuhu, visiting people from the three counties of Jing, Jingde, and Tai who are residing in Wuhu, inquiring about the disaster situation in those counties. The total amount of relief funds allocated to Anhui by the relief association is 150,000 yuan. Even if there is an increase in the future, it will be difficult to reach 300,000 yuan. With such a wide disaster area and such a severe disaster situation, it is feared that it will be a drop in the bucket and will not help. An appeal has been made to fellow villagers living abroad to donate more, so that disaster victims who are about to die can survive. In a subsequent conversation with reporters, it was stated that the standard for this relief distribution is to prioritize those who have suffered the most from both banditry and drought. After careful review, the first batch is 20 counties, including Jing and Tai, and the rest will be distributed in order. The disaster victims who receive relief should be over 50 years old, under 15 years old, or disabled, or those who cannot survive without relief. The principle of saving the dying but not the poor will be strictly enforced. After the investigators arrive in the disaster-stricken counties, they will go to the disaster area to conduct a thorough investigation to ensure speed. Each adult will receive one yuan, and each child will receive five jiao. Relief tickets will be issued directly to the disaster victims without the intervention of any organizations to avoid malpractice. Another review will be conducted, and then the investigator will jointly determine the location with the county government, distribute them by region, and issue them by name to avoid crowding. However, it is now the coldest period, and the beginning of spring is coming soon. The disaster victims are eagerly awaiting relief, so there can be no delay in Wuhu, and it has been decided to set off tomorrow morning. It is also reported that Jing County's fellow villagers in Wuhu have raised more than 10,000 yuan in relief funds, Jingde's fellow villagers have raised 6,000 yuan in relief funds, and Taiping's fellow villagers have raised 5,000 yuan in relief funds, all of which have been handed over to Zhu and others for distribution. Chief Master Hong San, the resident investigator in Anhui, seeing the vast disaster situation in southern Anhui, will come to Wuhu in the next few days to inspect various counties and supervise the distribution of relief by the investigators. (22nd)

Silk Mills Closing One After Another 80

This county has always been known as a region with developed industry and commerce, and there are numerous silk and yarn mills throughout the county. In recent years, silk mills have been unable to maintain production due to low silk prices and a sharp decline in foreign silk sales. Currently, only fifteen silk mills, such as Yongtai, are勉强 maintained, which is less than 40% compared to the peak period. As the end of the lunar year approaches, all the silk mills that are still operating are closing down one after another because the final closing period is approaching. Four mills, including Longchang, closed down yesterday, and the rest must close down by the end of this month at the latest.

Businesses of All Sizes Closing Down One After Another 81

In recent years, due to frequent natural disasters, the rural economy has collapsed, and urban commerce has also plummeted. Bankruptcies are caused by tight financial turnover. As the end of the lunar year approaches, the final settlement period is approaching, and stores with high debts are unable to maintain themselves. For example, Sanmao Dried Goods Store outside the South Gate, Sun Chunyang Tea Food Store at the North Suspension Bridge, Hangzhou Hengfeng Silk Factory on Tongyun Road, and Yongmao Clothing Store, Shunxing Noodle Restaurant, etc., have all closed down one after another in the past few days. Xinmeihua Shoe and Hat Foreign Goods Store, which was opened by Shen Yuting and his son, has been in business for more than ten years. Recently, due to slow business, it has been unable to maintain itself, so it stopped operating yesterday and hired lawyer Sun Xiangcheng as a representative to announce the liquidation and solicit bids. The sluggish state of society has reached its peak.

Xicheng Bus Accident Injures Pedestrian 82

Xing Heshang, a man from Bao'ying, 30 years old, came to Wuxi with his wife Xu a few years ago to make a living and moved to Changan Bridge in this county, where he opened Zhang Hengsheng Noodle Shop. The business was still good, so life was quite comfortable. However, at about 3 PM yesterday, Xing went to Baimuqiao and returned to the city. While passing by the bend near the Railway Hotel, a Xicheng long-distance bus sped towards him. The monk could not avoid it in time and was knocked down by the bus. The front wheel ran over Xing's left calf, causing the skin to break and the bones to shatter. His leg was crushed off, and blood flowed all over the ground, a terrible sight. The Xicheng Company knew that an accident had occurred and immediately sent Xing's child to the Brothers Hospital for treatment. According to Dr. Zhu, the injury was very serious, and even if he survived, he would become disabled.

Initial Snowfall in Xidi 83

Since the beginning of winter, the weather has been mild and warm. At the start of this month, continuous cloudy rain persisted for a long time, and broad beans and vegetables flowered and bore fruit in sunny spots, an abnormality rarely seen in plants. In recent days, the weather has turned cold, but there has been no snowfall. On the afternoon of the 25th, dark clouds gathered densely, blocking the sunlight, hinting at snow. By about 10 PM, auspicious snowflakes danced, melting upon touching the ground, ceasing after ten-odd minutes.

Unexpectedly, when the assistant abbot went to the room to retrieve the item, both the door lock and the desk lock had been destroyed. He immediately telegraphed Abbot Jingbo. Jingbo returned upon hearing the alarm. Upon checking, the foreign currency stored in the drawer had vanished. After questioning the caretaker thoroughly, he was considered highly suspicious and was planned to be handed over to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation in the coming days.

Zhenjiang 95

Settlement of Rickshaw Pullers' Dispute 96

Yangzhou 98

Bandits Rob Oil Mill, Shooting Mill Owner 99

Li Dehai Oil Mill in Wangjia Alley, about two miles from Shiqiao, Jiangdu, was attacked by a large group of bandits armed with guns at about 7 PM on the 24th. They forbade any outcry and ordered the mill owner, Li Fuyi, to hand over silver and cash. When Li hesitated in his response, they shot him in the head, piercing one eye, killing him instantly. They also shot and wounded Yan Shu, a mill worker. Simultaneously, the bandits divided into groups and went to Li's residence (diagonally opposite the oil mill), arbitrarily looting and stealing loot before fleeing with shouts. After inspecting the losses, it was found that 98 silver dollars, four jiao in small coins, 12,300 copper coins, and four pieces of men's and women's leather and cotton clothing were stolen from the oil mill. From the house, 130 silver dollars, 6,000 copper coins, a gold hairpin, a gold ear pick, a gold ring, and many pieces of men's and women's clothing were stolen. At the time, the local police station, citing insufficient police force, rushed to report to the Second Branch in Zhouzhou. While passing through Xinqiao Town, they encountered Director Tang Chuliang and Adjutant Zhao on patrol, who immediately led the police to rush to the scene. The bandits had already fled.

Qingjiang 100

Continued Interrogation in the Suppression of the Huai-Si Small Sword Society 101

More than a thousand members of the Small Sword Society in the Second District of Huaiyin have been suppressed by the two regiments of the Provincial Security Brigade and the security teams of the Huai and Si counties since the 20th of this month, and their momentum has been somewhat diminished. According to the county magistrate of Huaiyin, who returned to the city on the 22nd, after the Small Sword Society bandits were suppressed in Huai, a part of them fled to Siyang. On the morning of the 21st, the Second Regiment of the Provincial Security Brigade received a notice from the First Regiment and entered Huangxu, Siyang, to assist in the suppression. They engaged in battle in the area of the Twelfth Bao and Nanxinji in Siyang. Both sides exchanged heavy gunfire, killing more than 200 bandits. The First Regiment of the Provincial Security Brigade also engaged in a fierce battle with the bandits in Tianxu, Siyang, killing more than 100 bandits. The bandit side suffered heavy losses. Currently, all units are still in pursuit. However, the provincial government has telegraphed again, ordering the dispatch of more troops to suppress them in order to eliminate the bandit scourge permanently and ensure local peace.

Nantong 102

Ring Leader of Trafficking Women Arrested 103

Evil people trafficking humans are rampant in counties north of the Yangtze, and most of those lured are young women. Although government offices have investigated and arrested them and repeatedly uncovered organizations, the ringleader is a woman named Chen Jin Guniang. On the 26th, she was tracked down and arrested by bailiffs in Dongting, Wuxi, and taken to the court for interrogation and detention.

Prosecutor Appeals Lawyer's Seduction Case 104

Lawyer Wu Guixin, the current vice president of the Nantong Bar Association, was accused of seduction by his niece, Li Xiangzhi, in court. Prosecutor Wang Lansheng filed a public prosecution with the criminal court. The case caused a sensation throughout the county. Later, Wu and Li suddenly reached an understanding. At the end of the trial, Wu Guixin was declared innocent. Prosecutor Wang refused to accept the verdict, arguing that this case was not a private prosecution matter. Even if the victim could forgive, the law would not allow it. He appealed to the High Court. The High Court's Criminal Division has scheduled a hearing for February 12th.

Gaoyou 105

Robbery and Assault in Pingtiaozhuang 106

In Pingtiaozhuang, Jianshui Township, Eighth District, west of the lake in this county, seven or eight bandits suddenly arrived at about 1 AM last night. Each carried pistols and rifles. They first went to the home of farmer Yang Zhensan and broke in. The family members were awakened from their sleep. The bandits dragged Yang's wife from the bed, tied her with ropes, and poured kerosene on her, forcing her to reveal where the silver was hidden. After being doused, Yang's wife was on the verge of death. Helpless, the bandits searched everywhere, losing over a thousand yuan worth of silver dollars and valuables. The bandits were still not satisfied and went to the home of their neighbor, Yang Bolin. Yang had already woken up upon hearing the alarm, and he and his wife used their bodies to block the door. Unable to enter, the bandits fired two shots, both hitting Bolin's waist. He fell to the ground instantly, severely injured, and his life may be in danger.

Jiashan 107

Robbers Kill and Plunder 108

At the end of the lunar year, reports of robberies have been frequent in this county. Recent robbery cases are recorded below: 1. At about 11 PM last night, more than ten bandits, similar to salt smugglers, armed with sharp weapons, arrived at the home of farmer Wei Guihe in Xujiayanqiao, east of Zhanghui Town. Taking advantage of a gap, they escaped to the roof, where the bandits spotted them. They fired shots to threaten them. Startled, they fell from the roof. His wife, Shen, rushed out of the door, crying for help, and was shot by the bandits. As a result, she was shot three times, fell to the ground, and died. The loss was several thousand yuan. As the bandits were about to leave, they dropped a hat and several rifle bullets. Fei Gongxia, the director of the Fengjing Beizhen Public Security Bureau, together with the water patrol captain, went to the countryside to investigate and arrest the bandits. 2. In Fengjiadou, Tianren Village, more than ten robbers arrived at Shen Erguan's house the day before yesterday while they were husking rice. They shouted and wielded sharp weapons, broke down the door, and tied Erguan and his family members with hemp ropes. They looted and stole eight shi of white rice, clothes, and other items worth about 200 yuan. They spent an hour looting before leaving by boat.

Xiaoshan 109

Rural Bankruptcy and Commercial Decline 110

At the end of the year in Xiaoshan, due to rural bankruptcy, business in various industries is exceptionally sluggish. Even the loans made to the countryside have not been collected at all. For example, grocery stores rely entirely on receivables to repay other debts. Having encountered such a lean year, the receivables have been severely impacted, and many cannot even sustain themselves. Furthermore, the money shops, which were originally scheduled to close and cease payments on the 20th of the lunar calendar, have had to delay the settlement date due to uncollected receivables from various industries. It is estimated that the accounts can only be settled on the day before New Year's Eve. Moreover, there are more than twenty merchants who have closed down in both urban and rural areas, which shows the decline of commerce in Xiaoshan.

Special Article by Xu Daolin 111

Foe or Friend? (Continued) (Continued) 112

\[Review of Sino-Japanese Relations] 113

4. Errors in the Recognition of Contemporary Chinese Figures. The Japanese pride themselves on their ability to keenly observe and analyze figures, a skill in which they claim to surpass Westerners. However, when it comes to key Chinese figures, I have yet to see the Japanese make accurate assessments. Take, for example, the frequent commentaries on Mr. Chiang in publications like the Japan Diplomatic Times. In the Japanese commentary, Mr. Chiang is often compared with past Chinese figures such as Yuan Shikai and Li Hongzhang, which is truly an inappropriate analogy. Yuan Shikai and Li Hongzhang each have their place in Chinese history, and it is not necessary to discuss them here. However, Mr. Chiang and Yuan and Li lived in eras separated by at least a generation (in China, 30 years is considered a generation). Regardless of their different backgrounds, educations, or environments, the times in which they lived are absolutely different. Yuan and Li rose from the imperial era or the imperial examination era. Mr. Chiang, since his youth, had already participated in revolutionary organizations. For more than thirty years afterward, during the period of greatest malleability in life, he never left the revolutionary cause. His education and thought can be said to have been molded entirely by Mr. Sun Yat-sen. His life has never escaped the revolutionary environment. I do not believe that there are so-called supermen in the world. Everyone is influenced by the times and the environment. Mr. Chiang is who he is entirely because he grew up in a revolutionary environment. It can be said that there is not a single trace of the consciousness or habits of the pre-imperial era in his blood or mind. The distance between Mr. Chiang and Yuan and Li can be said to be like the distance between a modern Republic of China and a despotic state hundreds of years ago. They belong to two completely different eras and two completely different types. Comparing Mr. Chiang with Yuan and Li and using the habits and understanding of Yuan and Li to judge Mr. Chiang is truly as ridiculous as the Chinese saying, "Laozi and Han Fei are transmitted together." I assert that the Japanese have not really understood Mr. Chiang because they have not recognized the era and the figure. Therefore, they want to apply the methods previously used on the remnant figures of the imperial era to the present, hoping to achieve the same effect, which is obviously impossible. Let me give an example here. I am not a member of the Chinese Kuomintang, so of course I do not know the content and details of the Kuomintang's foreign policy. However, I know that the Kuomintang's so-called revolutionary foreign policy has its own unique and consistent strategy. After the Jinan Incident, I heard that Tan Yankai, the chairman of the National Government, questioned Chiang Kai-shek, the military commander at the time, "If you want to defend Jinan to the death, how can you withdraw the main force of the Northern Expedition? If you want to abandon Jinan, why leave a regiment of troops to defend Jinan to the death, and finally order them to withdraw?" Mr. Chiang replied, "This is the strategy of our revolutionary army. First, of course, we must show the revolutionary spirit of not yielding, and show that Jinan was forcibly occupied by Japanese troops, not abandoned by China itself. Second, we must consider the overall situation of the revolution and not hinder the progress of the Northern Expedition. Third, we must preserve the Chinese army and not make meaningless sacrifices. As long as Jinan resists for three days, the Japanese act of forceful occupation will be exposed to the world, then the purpose will have been achieved. Therefore, in the end, I ordered the regiment that was defending to the death to risk withdrawing, and let the outside world know that we wanted to use the strength of a regiment of men to confront the entire division of Fukuda." I observed Mr. Chiang's use of troops against Japan, from Shanghai, the Battle of the Great Wall, to the final withdrawal from the Battle of Miyun. It can be said that it is all a consistent spirit since the Jinan Incident. At least it can show that the revolutionary army cannot abandon any place where its strength lies without paying a price. Japan wanted to apply the precedent of easily obtaining Shenyang to all of China, but it is ultimately impossible. We have repeatedly studied Mr. Chiang's diplomatic policy toward Japan and recalled the opinion letter he issued in January of the 21st year of the Republic of China. We can see that his position on Japanese diplomacy is "no severance of relations, no declaration of war, no peace talks, no treaty." This diplomatic policy of his is completely consistent with his so-called defensive tactics of gradual resistance and the revolutionary strategy of being strong, unyielding, and adaptable, and it has never changed. However, this policy is not thorough, and some people in the country at the time strongly opposed it. But looking back now, one cannot help but say that this policy is relatively the only way out, because countries with unequal national and military strength can only use this policy and strategy to deal with each other. If Japan understands this principle, it should know that if Japan wants to threaten China again with force and obtain a result of submission, it can be said that it will not achieve its purpose. This is not because the revolutionary authorities have any ability that surpasses their predecessors, but simply because the times are different. In the past, in the imperial era or the warlord era, when encountering dangerous times, the authorities were afraid and submitted because of the concept of preserving their own interests and positions. Now, in the revolutionary period in China, the high degree of national consciousness no longer allows the authorities to have a single bit of selfishness. Since they have embraced the idea of "dying for the country" and "laying down their lives," what is there to fear or worry about? In the end, China's adoption of this revolutionary strategy and policy of "always ready to die, seeking survival at every step" will also lead Japan to the same fate.

5. Ignoring the Errors of Chinese National Mentality. Judging from the various steps Japan has taken towards China recently, one cannot help but say that "they are too eager to harm each other but too ignorant of each other." Japan, on the one hand, creates the false premise that the Chinese people can never compromise with Japan, and therefore believes that only by destroying the Chinese nation can Japan rest easy. Moreover, it believes that to destroy China, it must use extremely vicious means to prevent it from ever recovering. Regarding the first point, I dare to assert that there is no absolutely irreconcilable situation between China and Japan. It is not necessary to go far to find other examples. Just take China's relationship with Britain. The Chinese people, of course, must strive to struggle to obtain true independence and equality from the aggression of imperialism. Britain, as the leader of imperialism, has all the unequal treaties with China that arose from the Opium War against Britain. In the beginning, Britain harmed us with deadly toxins, and then bound us with inescapable chains. This is a deep-rooted hatred in the bones of the Chinese people. If it is said that China's deteriorating relations with Japan have a history of more than ten years since the Twenty-One Demands, then its deteriorating relations with Britain have a history of more than eighty years. However, in China today, it can be said that anti-British sentiment is not very strong. This is, of course, because Britain has recently changed its opium policy. The biggest reason is that Britain has not had any territorial ambitions toward China in recent decades. What it has been engaged in is only in the commercial and economic fields. Therefore, as long as many unequal treaties can be corrected, China is willing to be friends with Britain for economic mutual benefit. If Japan only recognizes this point, it will know that China does not have a hundred-generation hatred concept. Whether it likes or dislikes, friends or enemies, can be completely shifted by facts. If Japan can truly abandon the act of territorial aggression, China is still willing to take Western countries as friends, let alone Japan, which is of the same continent and the same race? The entire Japan, as an Eastern nation, should understand Eastern psychology. The characteristics of Easterners, especially the Chinese, are that they value emotions, integrity, etiquette, and morality. Now, Japan's estimation of China's territory has extremely damaged Chinese emotions and dignity. To prevent China from seeking revenge, it is taking actions that violate morality. Even if China wants to cooperate with Japan, how can it endure such a humiliating form of cooperation? Japan sees Sino-Japanese relations too pessimistically, thinking that there is no hope of recovery. Therefore, Japan wants to put China to death in order to guard against it. Under this policy, Japan, on the one hand, uses various methods to exhaust China. It not only uses military force, but also directly and indirectly allows unscrupulous people to disturb the legal order in various parts of China and destroy China's good customs, in order to seek China's current death. On the other hand, it does not hesitate to use extremely cruel methods, attempting to harm and cut off the future life of the Chinese nation. The sale of heroin in various parts of China is mostly operated by Japanese merchants, or at least Japanese officials allow it. China has suffered from the harm of opium, and the health of the nation has been destroyed. Even today, although it has restored feelings for Britain, this hatred will be difficult to erase its traces for hundreds of generations. Japan is now following suit, and the poisoning is becoming more intense, which will make it difficult for future generations of China to forget. In order to eliminate China's retaliatory power, Japan is now also using ignorant Chinese traitors or warlord bureaucrats to hate and harm Chinese intellectuals. It does not know that Chinese intellectuals can never be completely eliminated. On this day, Japan is using the lowest-level traitors. These traitors will also become a major disaster for Japan in the future. To renege on one's words is the same. Moreover, what Japan deeply dislikes is the method of the Communist Party, and what it advocates is the characteristics of the Eastern nation. Now, Japan often wants to use the past boring warlords and bureaucrats in China to create Japanese-style politics in various places or to become puppet regimes of Japan. This matter is causing the Chinese people to recall the situation of the Third International, which wanted to create Russian-style politics in Wuhan and Guangzhou. After all, do Guangzhou or Wuhan still have traces of this kind of politics forcibly created by foreign forces? Isn't it because the public was indignant, rose up to expel them, and it was like a flash in the pan? We dare to tell Japan that the behavior that is most difficult for any national with characteristics and national consciousness to endure is the desire to eliminate its national character and historical culture. Eastern nations are nations that value morality. Easterners should value Eastern habits and thoughts. All methods that violate morality, use violent coercion, and are close to hypocrisy and cruelty are not methods that Easterners fear to tolerate. If Japan does not want to sow deep hatred for generations in China, I think it should reflect on itself calmly.

In short, Japan's error lies in treating China in the midst of revolution as a normal country, in mistakenly recognizing the twentieth century as the eighteenth and nineteenth centuries and still adopting the methods or traditional policies of the previous century, in mistakenly recognizing revolutionary forces and treating them as remnants of the imperial era, in dealing with revolutionary strategies with the means of dealing with bureaucratic politics, and not realizing that Japan's military oppression can only coerce ignorant bureaucrats and warlords, but cannot subdue a nation whose nationalism is developing. On the other hand, it also considers the deterioration of relations between the two countries to be too pessimistic, and does not realize that it is not too far to stray. As long as it abandons military force and territorial aggression, it is very possible to improve the relations between the two countries and between the people.

6. Japanese Errors (2):：： 114

Errors in Indirect Measures

The errors in Japan's understanding of China have been discussed above. Now, I would like to further point out the fallacies in the measures Japan has taken in dealing with international affairs. Since this article is written to discuss Sino-Japanese relations, it is limited to those caused by the China issue.

1. The Error of Withdrawing from the League and Becoming Isolated Japan has created an irreversible situation in China. On the one hand, it rejects the advice of friendly countries, and on the other hand, it rejects the resolutions of the League of Nations, and even does not hesitate to withdraw from the League, which is a shocking move. As for Japan's own explanation, it is that Japan has its own independent stance. However, from an outsider's perspective, Japan verbally touts independence but actually achieves isolation. In fact, for Japan, independence is possible, but isolation is not. The current trend in the world is the trend of international cooperation. Almost no country is willing to be isolated outside of international groups. For example, regarding the League of Nations, the Soviet Union, a country with different doctrines, resolutely joined, and the United States also abandoned its traditional policy of non-cooperation and tended to join the League of Nations. Now Japan is in this period of withdrawing from international groups and is willing to be isolated. Tracing the reason, it is due to the desire to implement the annexation of Manchuria and Mongolia, the unification of East Asia, and the monopoly of the Pacific Ocean, but it does not know that it has completely fallen into the error of violating the trend of the times. In the world, only generally weak countries that have not yet completed the revolution have to advocate an independent stance and are willing to be isolated from international groups or treaties, because the national strength is unequal, and after joining, they cannot obtain equal status and interests, but only obligations and no rights, and it is better not to join; if in countries with an existing foundation, there is no one who voluntarily isolates themselves from international affairs. Before Japan withdrew from the League of Nations, it sought advice from senior officials and scholars, which shows that it also considered the issue to be serious, but it could not stop, and finally made a resolute decision. Since Hirota came to power, although he has appointed himself to replace the restraints of the League of Nations with separate negotiations, Japan has not hesitated to cast a dark shadow on world peace. At a time when international relations are becoming increasingly close, it has created a position of being watched by the world, which is ultimately not the benefit of Japan. (To be continued)

Fourth Batch 117

Silver dollars arrived in Shanghai this morning.

502,000 yuan shipped on the President Hoover.

The Bank of China and the Bank of Communications will send personnel to oversee the unloading.

According to the New News Agency, the member banks of the Foreign Exchange Equalization Committee, including the Central Bank of China, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications, purchased 20 million yuan of silver from Hong Kong to Shanghai to regulate the financial market. Three batches, totaling approximately 2 million yuan, have already been shipped and distributed according to the 4-4-2 ratio, deposited in the Central Bank of China, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications. According to the Foreign Exchange Equalization Committee, the fourth batch of silver dollars, totaling approximately 502,000 yuan, has been shipped to Shanghai on the Dollar Line's President Hoover. The ship is scheduled to enter the port and arrive in Shanghai at 7:00 AM this morning, docking at the Dollar Line pier in Bailianjing, Pudong. The Bank of China and the Bank of Communications will send personnel to clear customs and then hire laborers to unload the silver, transport it ashore, and store it in warehouses. It is also reported that the previous three batches of silver shipped to Shanghai have not been used, as there is sufficient silver in Shanghai and ample circulation in the market, so there is no need to use these silver dollars.

Philippine residents in the city will go to the port to welcome him.

Philippine Governor-General Murphy departed from Manila on the 23rd to go to Washington. In addition, the draft Philippine constitution, the procedures for establishing an autonomous government, US-Philippine economic and trade relations, the US High Commissioner to the Philippines, and all other issues are within the scope of Mr. Murphy's visit to the United States. Therefore, the mission he bears has a significant impact on the future situation in the Pacific and deserves our attention. According to a report from Dollar Lines, the President Hoover, carrying the Philippine Governor-General to the United States, will arrive here at around 8:00 AM on the 28th. The Philippine community in this port and the US Consulate General are preparing to welcome him. After arriving in Shanghai, Mr. Murphy will stay for one night and then depart on the same ship the next day to the United States. Accompanying Mr. Murphy are Mr. and Mrs. Weidiham, Norman Hale, Edward Cabot, and Secretary Ms. Benkana.
