Spring and Autumn

Xiaoxitian 219

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 8: Remote Place, Light Official, Arriving with Strong Opinions; Grand Hall, Lavish Banquet, Outside There are Pitiful Creatures

I took people to examine the body, but the garrison soldiers on the city gate actually wouldn't let me go. I jumped up and down, saying: I am the magistrate of this county, a person died right outside my door, I'm just taking a look myself, it's my own business, is it any of your concern? Unless you beat me to death, I won't leave. The soldiers had no choice but to let me through. I saw several rope marks on the dead man's neck, he was obviously strangled to death. I searched the dead man's body and found two letters, proving that he was a traveler from elsewhere. Since he was a traveler from elsewhere, he must have stayed at an inn in this county. So I gathered all the innkeepers in the county and asked if the dead man was a guest at their establishment. The truth finally came out, the innkeeper only said that he had left the inn while ill, not daring to reveal the fact that the army had strangled him. Later, I threatened to beat the innkeeper to death, and he finally told the truth. I couldn't hold back my anger and went to find the commander. He was lying in bed smoking opium, and said with a smile: Magistrate Zhou, you are meddling too much. What does it matter if a few ordinary people die? The important matter of military pay, I have asked for repeatedly, but you never provide it. A person died outside the city, a trivial matter, even if you didn't care, no one would ask you, what does it have to do with you? What does it have to do with me? Yet you come to see me. Gentlemen, do you think these are the words a human would say? Yet he was just a minor commander. I still haven't been able to get over this, I just feel sorry for the dead man. Secondly, it's about them wanting money. Originally, the provincial government had made very thorough preparations, sending a financial commissioner to that area, with all the finances of several counties being centrally collected and distributed, and pay being issued by the financial commissioner, not involving the county magistrate. But those soldiers couldn't wait from one month to the next, and would demand money from the financial commissioner before the due date. The financial commissioner couldn't conjure up money either, so he came to find the county magistrate. This time, the commissioner brought a company commander and twenty or thirty soldiers, suddenly descending upon the county office, demanding that I hand over twenty thousand dollars within three days. According to the old custom, when a county magistrate encountered such a disaster, he would gather all the village chiefs from the county, and have them tied up and beaten one by one. (123)

Paying Tribute at the Tomb of the Martyrs of the January 28th Incident 220

— Chen Liang

Silently, without a sense of joy, without a sense of grief, it is an emotional void.

I pay tribute to the martyrs of the January 28th Incident with a bouquet of plain-colored daffodils, a cup of light-flavored clear wine, and a sincere heart. I do not feign sorrow, nor do I shed a single tear of the weak. Calmly, calmly let the hot blood flow calmly within my skin. I am not afraid of the piercing cold of the wilderness, nor the knife-like north wind. I just clench my two firm fists, and quietly lower my head.

Yellow tomb soil, withered vines, ah, martyrs; the flower of national glory irrigated by your blood will never wither. I can still vaguely remember, it was a dream, who were those people? Covered in blood, they dragged their blood-stained swords in battle, singing, that voice... without sorrow, without regret, the brave melody moved me. They waved to me and said: Come over, we are all pioneers of the nation! Never having known each other in life, we can naturally meet after death. Then I woke up. Ghost, I feel the blood all over my body becoming even hotter.

Martyrs! You have all died before us, you shouted under the bombs raining from the sky, you charged in the forest-like ranks of Type 38 rifles, for the sake of the Chinese nation, not hesitating to use your chests to resist the enemy's bayonets, blood, flowing, flowing in Zhuyuantun, flowing in Miaohang, flowing in Jiangwan,... As for the enemy, the heads of those enemies have also rolled under the knives of our brave warriors. Hehe! Heroes of the nation. Your resistance this time has made all the imperialists show some restraint. The fish and meat in their eyes have turned into a piece of steel.

Martyrs! I no longer want to say more about your great achievements before your spirits. I should not grieve for your deaths for the glory of the nation, and at the same time, I should not excessively praise your merits, because this is all fulfilling the greatest duty for the nation. It is the responsibility that all of us who die later should fulfill.

I put the daffodils on the tombstone, I moisten the tomb with light wine, I hope that the warm season will arrive early, and that green grass sprouts and blood-colored wildflowers re-emerge on the martyrs' tombs. Clenching two firm fists, silently looking up at the sky, the sky is blue, the sun is white, an emotional void.

Tidbits 221

— (Qifenglou Master)

The ancients said, "In the fourth month in the countryside, there are few idle people." I say, "In the city at the end of the year, everyone is busy." Don't you see? In recent days, the pedestrians in the market, those buying New Year's goods, those delivering New Year's gifts, and those finishing up all the affairs of the New Year, are bustling and hustling, much more than usual, and the goods sold in the stores are cheaper and cheaper, with extra gifts added. They are all making a final struggle in the fleeting end of the year, a momentary shout!

Shanghai is a Big Dye Vat 222

— Zhou Xian

I have a younger cousin whose family circumstances aren't very good, so after he graduated from junior high school, we scrambled around to send him to Shanghai, where he was admitted to the high school affiliated with a certain university.

When my cousin first came to Shanghai, he had a "Tokyo head," a hairstyle that had been popular in Shanghai a dozen years ago. He wore a free-cloth long gown and white cotton socks with black cloth-soled shoes.

After being in Shanghai for only a month, he let his hair grow longer. Then, he started wearing his Zhongshan suit-style school uniform as everyday clothes, and stuffed his free-cloth long gown into the bottom of a trunk. At the same time, he replaced his white cotton socks with patterned ones, and his black cloth-soled shoes with basketball shoes.

After one semester, his hair was combed back and he was applying snow cream to his face. He wore a serge long gown and Western-style trousers. He only wore basketball shoes at school, and leather shoes when he went out.

Starting from the third semester, he began to wear Western suits bought and altered on Wusong Road. White shirts, patterned ties, neatly combed hair, a fair face—you couldn't tell he was a young man from the countryside; he actually looked like a city person.

At the same time, he started going to cafes, movie theaters, and sometimes even slipped into dance halls. On the other hand, he even started flirting with girls.

After muddling through another semester, my cousin suddenly dropped out of school. At first, I thought it was because of financial problems. One day, my uncle came to Shanghai and talked about it, and I learned that the reason for dropping out was partly due to the financial burden, but mostly because my cousin had a girlfriend in Shanghai and wanted to break off his engagement with his fiancée.

I couldn't help but sigh and say, "Shanghai is a big dye vat!"

Old Wounds Still Ache 223

The Fragrant Mists of the Imperial Incense 224

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Regarding the elimination of superstition, Guangxu and I shared the same view, but to avoid any unexpected unfortunate events, I was unwilling to express it too openly, so I had to respond with a diplomatic, rounded tone. "Apart from this, I really can't express anything else! I wonder what Your Majesty thinks?" "These are ridiculous superstitious tales!" Guangxu was unwilling to be subtle at all. Because he knew that among all the people he saw in the palace, whether high or low, almost everyone would secretly report his words and actions to the Empress Dowager; even Empress Longyu was unreliable. There was only one exception, and that was me. So he dared to speak frankly to me. "Last year, there was another matter that perhaps you didn't know about. That is, on the day of the ancestral temple sacrifice, I seemed to hear some relatively interesting news, and I couldn't help but feel more excited than usual. So at the end of the sacrificial ceremony, I deliberately stood in front of the incense table, straightened my body, raised my right hand, gave a salute commonly used by foreigners, and said at the same time, 'Ancestors, please look at the foreigner's salute. Is it good or not?' This was originally just to amuse myself, and there was no disrespect to the ancestors. If they really had spirits, they certainly wouldn't be offended. But several eunuchs standing near me heard it early on. It wouldn't have mattered if only they had heard it; it just so happened that there was such a coincidental thing in the world, on that very night, probably because the incense and candles burned during the day had not been completely extinguished, they actually rekindled and spread, and by the time the guards discovered it, one corner of the ancestral temple was already on fire. Fortunately, there were many people and they desperately poured water to extinguish it, only then was this important building preserved. As a result, those eunuchs who were most superstitious began to discuss it." (233)

Statistics of a Lifetime of Time 225

— (Hanwen)

A person born into the world, living an average of seventy-three years, the statistics are startling. An expert has done precise calculations, which are quite interesting, and are specially recorded below.

Sleep takes up twenty-two years and six months.

Work takes up twenty years and four months.

Being sick in bed takes up four years and two months.

Eating and drinking takes up one year and six months.

Entertainment takes up five years and six months.

Getting haircuts takes up one year and four months.

Bathing takes up two years and eight months.

Resting takes up four years and five months.

Talking to people takes up two years and seven months.

Walking and traveling takes up four years and nine months.

Socializing takes up one year and five months.

Everything else takes up one year and ten months.

Places Visited

A Trip to Cuiwei Peak 226

— Xuxin

Since the recovery of Ningdu, I have been stationed with the army in the city for more than a month. The remote small town has no places for leisure, and I am extremely bored. A local said: About eight miles northwest of the city, there is Cuiwei Peak, which is quite famous in the history of bandit suppression. Why not take a trip there? However, the mountain is steep and not easy to climb. In recent days, Shanghai newspapers have also carried special dispatches for several days, reporting that Chairman Xiong of Jiangxi and others have visited Cuiwei Peak by car on a certain day. Seeing that the authorities and gentlemen have patronized it, then perhaps the place is indeed worth a visit? So, three days after New Year's Day, I asked a guide and, together with colleagues Mr. Huang Mutao, Mr. Zhang Ying, and young Mr. Zhang Gongren, walked out of the north gate and followed the motor road. This road was recently built and can lead directly to the foot of the mountain. At the end of the road, a wooden archway is erected, with the words "Cuiwei Peak" written on it, a newly constructed structure. Upon entering, the mountain shape unfolds like two hands, embracing an open space in the middle. Observing its atmosphere, it is already extraordinary. Inside, there are several acres of fields, and next to the fields there is a stream, its sound gurgling. Walking only a few dozen steps, a large rock face rises abruptly, strange and majestic, like a giant mansion, like a pillar of heaven, standing in the way, with a myriad of forms. Turning to the west, the mountain road becomes higher and higher. Along the way, there are several cliffs, one east and one west, with only enough space for one person in between. We then stooped and followed the road through the gap, trudging upwards. Having passed the jagged rocks, the road begins to diverge. The guide said: Those who wish to ascend the Crimson Fortress of Cuiwei Peak must go to the right; those who wish to go to the Gold Essence Cave of Cuiwei Peak must turn to the left. At this time, we had already reached the mountainside from the foot of the mountain, and we felt breathless and drenched in sweat. So we rested briefly at the crossroads and discussed for a moment. Because climbing the Crimson Fortress is even more difficult than going to the Gold Essence Cave, we decided to seize the opportunity and advance to the more difficult place first. Before long, the so-called Crimson Fortress, the highest point of Cuiwei Peak, was towering in the middle of the sky, standing firmly in front of us. Viewed from the front, it is a huge rock, dark and strangely beautiful, how can it be just a thousand cliffs! Ding Shi said, "The peak marks outside the rainbow, the ridge is placed among the white clouds, the tilted wall suddenly stands upright, the absolute peak is isolated and round," which can be imitated. We thought that if we had already climbed this peak but did not reach its peak and returned in disappointment, it would be too lacking in courage, so we all climbed up the rocks. With our chests against one wall and our hands supporting another, imitating the ascent of apes, we zigzagged in the rock crevices, sometimes bright and sometimes dark, pausing every five steps and panting every ten steps. Thus, we were careful, as if climbing a dangerous plank road, as if climbing a ladder to heaven, for half an hour. Suddenly, we felt a cool breeze and a refreshing atmosphere. Crossing a "Heavenly Gate," we had reached its summit. So we were very happy and lingered on its top. It is about a hundred steps long and half as wide. In the middle stands a flagpole, and the national flag flutters in the sky. There is nothing else except a few places of rotten grass and dilapidated walls, abandoned in the wilderness. The guide said: In December of the nineteenth year of the Republic of China, during the Ningdu 26th Route Army mutiny, wealthy households in the city and countryside, avoiding the scourge of the Red bandits, mostly built huts here. The rotten grass and dilapidated walls are the temporary dormitories of the past. The guide then pointed to the peak on the right and said, "Yellow Bamboo Fortress," and on the left, "Guanyin Fortress," forming five fortresses in total. The terrain is all naturally dangerous. The local militia in the fortresses do not need to fire their guns when encountering bandits. They only need to throw large stones down, and they can annihilate many bandits. Therefore, although the Red bandits tried their best to besiege, they could not break through in one or two years. However, although each fortress stored extremely abundant grain, the wealthy people loved gold, and it was better to hide gold. Gold, silver, and jewels could not satisfy hunger. After one or two years of support, the grain was exhausted, and the people ate tree bark and grass leaves, but Ningdu had not yet been recovered. Of the people in the fortresses, except for several hundred who broke out and escaped, it is unknown how many starved to death. In June of the twenty-first year, after Guanyin Fortress and the other small fortresses were breached, the mutual supporting momentum was lost, but only this Crimson Fortress had not yet been breached. In December, the bandits used a false plan to deceive the wealthy households in the Crimson Fortress to go down the mountain, and then they tied them up one by one and killed more than two hundred, a tragic event! In those years, the Central Army also once sent planes to carry flour and salt to provide relief, but the throws were not accurate and were seized by the bandits, which was truly a pity! We sat and talked for a long time, and then climbed down again, turned back to the crossroads, passed the side of a bunker, and went to the Gold Essence Cave. The cave is behind the Crimson Fortress, lower than that fortress. In front of it is a pond, and most of the drinking water for the fortresses is supplied from this. The cave is composed of natural large rocks. Next to the cave are carved four large characters, "Gold Essence Victory." There is also the Little Spiritual Official Temple. Upon entering the cave, it is suddenly spacious and bright, mountain flowers blooming, and tree birds chirping. The rock surrounds three sides, especially the rock extending out to the right, half-covering the sky, leaning forward and downward, about dozens of steps long. Stalactites hang upside down, like layers and shavings, like screens, extremely magnificent and strangely beautiful. The guide said: This was the granary of those who avoided the bandits in the past. At this time, the sun was already setting in the west, and people were also slightly tired, so we returned with our interest exhausted.

Repairing the Temple and Tomb of Confucius 231

Architectural Expert has been Hired

Mr. Liang Sicheng, son of Liang Rengong

Regarding the matter of repairing the Temple and Tomb of Confucius, in addition to the Internal Affairs and Education Departments each dispatching a section chief, the Executive Yuan also ordered the two departments to jointly hire an expert who has researched ancient architecture. Now the two departments have jointly hired Mr. Liang Sicheng, son of Liang Rengong. After graduating from Tsinghua University, Mr. Liang specialized in architecture in the United States and has extensively researched ancient Oriental architecture. He is currently the director of the Legal Style Group of the Beiping Construction Society. It is expected that he will meet with the two section chiefs, Tang Zhong, dispatched by the Internal Affairs and Education Departments, in Jinan by early February to conduct a comprehensive survey of Qufu.

Results of the Shandong Middle School Normal School Joint Examination Announced 232

486 Passed

260 to Retake

140 to Repeat a Grade

Jinan Correspondence: The provincial middle school student graduation joint examination has been held four times. The twenty-third year's winter session should be the fifth. And it also included the normal school student graduation joint examination. It was held on the 8th of this month. 886 students actually took the test. As a result of the exam, 486 passed, 260 failed one or two subjects and should retake the exam, and 140 failed three subjects and should repeat a grade. All the test papers were collected in one place, and the examination committee reviewed and calculated the scores overnight. The list of students who passed was only announced on the 26th. In this joint examination, the performance of the normal school students was very good. Those middle school students who passed with excellent results will still be handled according to the usual practice, and book coupons will be awarded. Those who rank at the top will be allowed to enter higher schools without examination. The reward methods for normal school students who pass are: 1) Handling according to the reward method for outstanding students in the middle school graduation joint examination, 2) Those with particularly excellent results will be introduced to work by the Education Department, and those who pass will be given priority for employment by the counties.

Saint Francis Xavier's College Plans to Build a New School 236

Saint Francis Xavier's College, located on Nansun Road in Hongkou, has been run by French clergy for 60 years. Upon investigating the internal organization of the school, it was found that it has a Chinese department and a Western department. In recent years, considering the increasing number of Chinese students applying to the school, the school staff had already resolved to build a new school for the Chinese department. As early as 1913, they had started planning to separate the Chinese and Western departments and establish separate schools. However, due to the impact of the war, the plan was shelved. Nevertheless, the number of applicants increased daily, and every year, hundreds of new applicants were turned away due to limited enrollment. Therefore, the school staff deeply regretted this. In 1922, despite the poor economic conditions, they launched the first fundraising campaign, raising 18,775 taels of silver. The following year, the students at the school continued the fundraising efforts, raising another 31,581 yuan. Later, alumnus Cheng Yize generously donated 10,000 taels of silver. At the same time, graduates from 1914 initiated the organization of a branch school to accommodate the new applicants from previous years, increase revenue, and expedite the realization of the new school in the shortest possible time. Thus, this branch school was established in February 1923. Initially, it only rented old-fashioned buildings on Seward Road in the city for two and a half years before moving to the current Western-style building on Rue Tenant de la Tour. This location can accommodate 350 students, hence the current enrollment of over 750 students. As for the funds raised earlier, they were used to purchase a 37-mu plot of land at the end of Tangshan Road (currently the school's temporary sports field) for over 100,000 taels of silver. The shortfall was covered by the school's operational funds. At that time, the area was mostly residential, so it was decided in 1927 to start construction. However, the construction was halted due to the Northern Expedition. Now, the surrounding area has transformed from a residential area into a factory area, which is not suitable for establishing a school. Therefore, the latest plan is to sell the land first and purchase a new, more suitable location. Thus, they are launching another fundraising campaign during this 60th-anniversary celebration, hoping that the new school can be completed as soon as possible.

Zhaohe Middle School Changes Principal 237

The Board of Directors Publicly Elects Yang Hu to Serve Concurrently

The Transfer of Authority Between the Old and New Principals Was Completed Yesterday

Mr. Yang Also Plans to Formulate a Plan to Improve School Affairs

Zhaohe Middle School in this city was originally established to commemorate the Zhaohe warship uprising in 1915. After the vice chairmen of the board, Wu Tiecheng, Yang Hu, Yu Qiaqing, and other members painfully managed the school, they got vigorous support from leaders from all walks of life in society, such as Wu Xingya, Du Yong, Huang Jinrong, and Chen Qun. Since its establishment, the school has already achieved a certain scale. Now, the board of directors of the school, in order to seek the school's own development, held a meeting to discuss and unanimously agreed that the initiator and vice chairman of the board, Mr. Yang Hu, has a glorious history in the Zhaohe uprising. It is appropriate for him to preside over the school. Mr. Yang also believes that education is one of the social undertakings and cannot refuse the role, so he immediately agreed to go to the school to take charge. The transfer of authority between the old and new principals was completed yesterday. It is heard that Mr. Yang has formulated a meticulous plan for improvement in order to seek development. It is also heard that the entrance examination for students who want to transfer to the school in the spring semester is scheduled for February 1st. There are still vacancies, and those who are interested in studying at the school can go to register.

Development of Guangdong East Middle School 238

Guangdong East Middle School in this city, formerly known as Guangzhao Middle School, is building new school buildings on Guangzhong Road and Shuidian Road at the end of North Sichuan Road. The existing land base is over 110 acres. The first phase of the project includes eight buildings in total, including an auditorium, office building, classrooms, gymnasium, dormitory, and dining hall. The project is expected to be completed at the beginning of next month, suitable for the start of the spring semester. A library is still in the planning and construction phase. The school is scheduled to hold the second new student entrance examination on February 7th at the original site of Yokohama Bridge, and the opening ceremony will be held at the new school on the 10th. The school's past junior high school graduation examination results have been excellent. This year's results even meet the first item of the Education Bureau's award standards, and the Education Bureau will award the bonus according to the regulations. It can be seen that the school's spirit and form are both excellent.

Shanghai Physical Education Association 252

Founders' Meeting Held Yesterday

Deadline of One and a Half Months to Complete Preparations

The Shanghai Physical Education Association, initiated by people in the sports and social education circles of this city, held its first founders' meeting at the Municipal First Public Sports Ground at 2 pm yesterday to discuss the draft charter and elect the preparatory committee. The details are recorded as follows:

Founders Present: Pan Gongzhan, Jiang Huaisu, Lu Lihua, Murakami Fei, Ding Shouting, Yuan Zengyu, Wang Keyong, Xiang Xianggao, Wang Zhuangfei (representing Xiang), Ma Chonggan, Qu Yue, Hu Zongfan, Lü Hailan, Shao Rugeng (representing Wang), Sun Hebin, Chen Yuze, Chen Mengyu, Zhang Longhai, Zong Xiaojie, Yu Ziyu, Yu Zian, and other 20 people.

Chairman's Report: Chairman Pan Gongzhan, Recorder Ding Shouting, first the chairman reported briefly, this association was jointly initiated by people in the sports industry, approved by the Municipal Party Department to organize, regarding this organization, there is now the China National Physical Education Association, which is to help the government guide national sports affairs, under which there are only regional organizations such as North China, South China, East China, and Central China. When the National Games were held in Beijing the year before last, it was suggested that there should also be physical education associations in various places to help local governments carry out sports affairs. Shanghai's sports undertakings have always been quite developed, and it is felt that there is a need for such an organization. This year's National Games will be held in Shanghai on Double Ten Day, so after soliciting the opinions of colleagues in the sports industry, the Shanghai Physical Education Association was initiated and organized to help the government develop Shanghai's sports undertakings.

Election of Preparatory Committee: Then, Wang Keyong, Ma Chonggan, Qu Yue, Hu Zongfan, Yuan Zengyu, Li Dachao, Jiang Huaisu, Shao Rugeng, Ding Shouting, Chen Mengyu, Lu Lihua, Du Yufei, Yu Ziyu, Chen Yuze, Xiang Xianggao, Sun Gebin, Chen Songchun, and other 17 people were elected as members of the preparatory committee to organize the preparatory meeting, and Wang Keyong was designated as the convener of the first meeting. The preparatory period was set to one and a half months.

Adoption of Draft Charter: The draft charter was then adopted as follows: Chapter 1 General Provisions, Article 1 The name of this association is the Shanghai Physical Education Association. Article 2 This association aims to study physical education, promote amateur sports, improve citizens' health, and promote the national spirit. Article 3 The address of this association is temporarily located at the Municipal First Public Sports Ground on Daji Road. Article 4 The tasks of this association are as follows: 1. Promote the implementation of universal physical training for men and women throughout the city. 2. Preside over amateur sports games throughout the city in accordance with all education laws and regulations promulgated by the central government and this city. 3. Assist in holding city sports games. 4. Assist the city's education bureau in developing and preparing various sports undertakings. 5. Assist various institutions, groups, schools, or individuals in conducting research and promotion of physical training. 6. Other matters that are consistent with the purpose of this association. Chapter 2 Membership, Article 5 The membership of this association is divided into the following two types: 1. Individual members, 2. Group members. Article 6 Any individual or group that agrees with the purpose of this association, has two or more members of this association introduce them, completes the membership procedures, and passes the review of the board of directors may become a member of this association. Article 7 Any person with one of the following circumstances may not be an individual member of this association: 1. Those who have been deprived of public rights and have not yet been restored, 2. Those who are legally incapacitated, 3. Those who have bad character, 4. Those who have bad habits, 5. Those who have been proven by a doctor's examination to have infectious diseases. Article 8 Groups or schools that have not been approved by the competent authority for filing or registration may not be group members of this association. Article 9 The representative of the group member of this association is one to two people per group. However, those with one of the circumstances in Article 7 may not be representatives of group members. Article 10 Individual members and representatives of group members of this association have the right to elect and be elected. Article 11 If a member of this association fails to pay membership fees for more than one year, fails to comply with the articles of association and resolutions of this association, or has any behavior that damages the reputation of this association, and it is verified to be true, the board of directors may resolve to cancel their membership. Chapter 3 Organization Article 12 The organization of this association is divided into three types: members' meeting, board of directors, and board of supervisors. Article 13 The board of directors is composed of 15 to 19 directors and 5 to 7 alternate directors, who are responsible for executing all internal and external affairs this year. The board of directors shall mutually elect three executive directors to handle daily affairs. Article 14 The board of supervisors is composed of 5 to 7 supervisors and 2 alternate supervisors, who are responsible for supervising all internal and external affairs of this association. The supervisors shall mutually elect one person as the executive supervisor. Article 15 The board of directors may set up the following groups: 1. General Affairs Group, 2. Research Group, 3. Promotion Group. Article 16 In order to promote business, this association may, upon resolution of the board of directors, hire enthusiastic supporters of this association as directors, and may set up special committees. Chapter 4 Staff, Article 17 The director of the Shanghai Education Bureau is the natural director of this association. The remaining directors, supervisors, and alternate supervisors are elected by the members' meeting from all members by means of a signed continuous election voting method. Those with more votes are elected. Directors and supervisors, when they leave their posts, are successively filled by alternate directors and supervisors. They are all voluntary positions. Article 18 Each group is headed by a director, who is concurrently held by the directors. Each group has a number of staff members, who are appointed by the board of directors from among the members to be responsible for the affairs of each group. They are all voluntary positions. Article 19 The term of office of directors and supervisors is three years, and they may be re-elected. Article 20 This association may discretionarily set up paid staff. Chapter 5 Meetings, Article 21 The members' meeting of this association is held every six months in spring and autumn, convened by the board of directors. Article 22 The members' meeting of this association requires the attendance of one-third of all members to be a legal quorum. Its resolutions are passed by a majority of the members present. Article 22 The board of directors meets once a month, convened by the executive directors. The board of supervisors meets once every two months, convened by the executive supervisor. Chapter 6 Funding, Article 23 The funding of this association is provided by the following: 1. Membership fees and annual fees, 2. Government subsidies, 3. Special fees. Article 24 Members pay fees as follows: 1. Individual members pay an admission fee of one yuan and an annual fee of one yuan, 2. Group members pay an admission fee of one yuan per representative and an annual fee of five yuan. Article 25 The income and expenditure of this association shall be reported and announced every six months. Chapter 7 Appendix.

How to Popularize Scientific Medicine in China (Part 1) 262

— Lecture by Yu Yunxiu, Recorded by Jiang Huiming

Since this publication began soliciting reports on medical and health conditions from various regions, the submitted articles often describe the situation as being in its rudimentary stages or just beginning to sprout. This is deeply regrettable! In the winter of the 23rd year of the Republic, our school held a Mandarin speech contest on the topic of "How to Popularize Scientific Medicine in China." We were fortunate to have Mr. Yu Yunxiu as the judge, who summarized the arguments of the various speakers and provided a final evaluation that was highly relevant and timely. This article is based on Mr. Yu's comments, which are not only insightful and incisive but also enlightening! In particular, his enumeration of the reasons for the underdevelopment of medicine and health in our country, his analysis of the root causes, and his exposure of the problems can be described as hitting the nail on the head and providing a vivid depiction! Therefore, we are publishing it in this journal to serve as a guide for those responsible for improving Chinese medicine and health. Reporter's note from Southeast Medical College, Shanghai.

The topic of your speeches today is: "How to Popularize Scientific Medicine in China." Most of your speeches take the view that popular education is a prerequisite for popularizing scientific medicine. I believe that simply starting with popular education is not useful. Consider the current elementary and secondary school teachers, university professors, and important figures in the government and the party. When they get sick, don't they still ask traditional doctors to treat them? Can it be said that their rationality is insufficient? Based on this fact, I believe that popular education is the backing for popularizing scientific medicine in China, not a prerequisite. The fundamental problem is that people with knowledge lack the ability to distinguish right from wrong and the will to consistently uphold their beliefs.

One student mentioned that a certain important figure in the Nationalist Government still consults traditional doctors when he is ill. Another mentioned the reform of old and new medicine in Japan, which I think is a good comparison. Since the Meiji Restoration, the development of scientific medicine in Japan has relied entirely on political power. The reason why scientific medicine cannot be popularized in China is that it lacks political power. Politics and medicine are closely linked.

We know that before the Meiji Restoration, traditional Chinese medicine dominated the medical scene in Japan. How was it possible to rapidly transform after the Meiji Restoration, abolish traditional Chinese medicine, and revive scientific medicine, unlike in China, where we are still hesitating and unable to move forward? The biggest reason is that the traditional Chinese medicine community in Japan had already begun to question the theories of Yin-Yang and the Five Elements. Scholars such as Goto Konzan, Kagawa Shūkei, and Yoshimasu Tōdō emphasized empiricism and opposed the traditional Yin-Yang and Five Elements theories, considering them to be abstract and useless. Kagawa's book is called "Selection of Medicines," and Yoshimasu's book has been collected and published as "Complete Works of Tōdō." It is truly a groundbreaking work in traditional Chinese medicine. You can refer to it. One part is called "Evidences of Medicines," in which he uses practical observation and description to deduce the effects of medicines, completely ignoring the theories of five colors matching the five internal organs and the five elements matching the five colors – the absurd theory that the spleen corresponds to earth and the kidney corresponds to water. Moreover, he frequently refutes the Yin-Yang and Five Elements theories. Goto died in 1733, and Yoshimasu died in 1771, both in the 18th century. At that time, they already had the idea of eliminating empty talk and moving towards practicality, and these two had many disciples. Yoshimasu Tōdō was even more famous and had more disciples. His doctrines spread throughout the country, and people of all levels, including feudal lords and officials, admired his doctrines. Therefore, political figures had a considerable degree of awareness. As a result, after the introduction of Dutch medicine, it was easy to accept it through the use of political power. After the Meiji Restoration, political figures adopted a clear principle, recognized the facts, and saw that Western medicine had a basis for every word and name. They simply used decisive measures to completely abolish traditional Chinese medicine, thus achieving the popularization of scientific medicine and reaching the second position in the world of medicine today. From this point of view, this is all due to the influence of Tōdō's doctrines and the political power that achieved medical reform!

Corpse Dissection: The Only Basis for Conclusive Medical Judgments 263

— Song Guobin

The case of Dr. Yin Leren of Nantong being accused of medical malpractice has lasted for over half a year. The Nantong District Court initially sentenced the defendant to a fine of 1,000 yuan. Dr. Yin, dissatisfied with the verdict, appealed to the High Court. To clarify the truth of the case, the High Court requested an assessment from the Zhenru Institute of Forensic Medicine. The main points of the institute's response were: (1) Whether there were a sufficient number of assistants present during the surgery; (2) It is common for needles to break suddenly during spinal puncture surgery, but whether this is sufficient to cause death depends on the location of the broken needle. If the broken needle is between the vertebrae or outside the spine, there is no reason for it to cause death. If the broken needle is between the vertebrae and inside the spinal cord, it can migrate to other locations. This can only be clarified through autopsy. The above two points are the most reasonable and fair assessment, and the phrase "This can only be clarified through autopsy" is particularly meaningful. Please elaborate on it.

In recent years, medical malpractice lawsuits have become increasingly common. When dealing with such cases, courts occasionally seek assessments from medical institutions in various regions as a reference for their judgments. However, the assessments are ultimately based on the facts described in the documents submitted, without the assessors having personally witnessed the situation. Disease resides within the human body, and doctors treat patients. Unfortunately, if a patient dies, whether this is due to the doctor's negligence cannot be determined solely by the speculation of a third party. To achieve complete clarity and convince both sides, it is necessary to dissect the deceased patient's body and conduct a thorough examination. In the well-publicized Yin case, according to the opinion of the Institute of Forensic Medicine, the crux of the matter is whether the broken needle was located between the vertebrae or inside the spinal cord. This conclusion is extremely accurate, but whether it was between the vertebrae or inside the spinal cord is not known to outsiders and cannot be determined by mere words. If the court, based on this statement, declares the defendant innocent, the patient's family may find it difficult to accept. Conversely, if the defendant is found guilty of negligent homicide, Dr. Yin can ask the judge how he knows that the broken needle was inside the spinal cord. All of these are extremely difficult issues to resolve. The only solution is to dissect the deceased's body to seek complete clarity. Once the body is dissected, the location of the broken needle can be easily determined, and previous doubts can be dispelled.

The purpose of litigation is to seek true right and wrong. Therefore, judges should base their judgments on accurate facts. The true evidence in medical cases lies in the deceased's body. Abandoning the patient's body and relying solely on the empty talk of pleadings or oral arguments will not reveal the truth. Therefore, in my opinion, if medical malpractice cases occur in the future, the court should make autopsy of the deceased's body the first priority. If the patient's family refuses the autopsy, the judge should refuse to accept the case. In this way, the court can achieve twice the result with half the effort, and both the plaintiff and defendant can save unnecessary arguments and obtain the true right and wrong. For the patient's family, if they are willing to sacrifice the remains of the deceased, they can vent their anger for a time. Otherwise, it is best to settle the matter peacefully.

Chinese Medicine and Health in the Past Year (Part 4) 264

— Jiang Huiming

Introduction｜Medical Education｜Medical Group Activities｜Medical Disputes｜Medical Publishing｜Medical Investigation｜Medical Construction｜Military Medical Training｜Glimpses of Traditional Medicine｜Trends in the New Pharmaceutical Industry｜Rural Health Surveys｜Urban Health Perspectives｜Conclusion

(12) Urban Health Perspectives

Urban health in China, such as in Shanghai, Beijing, Nanjing, etc., although they have initial models, seems to have progressed more in Shanghai. In the spring of the 23rd year of the Republic, the Anti-Tuberculosis Association initiated by Shanghai medical celebrities and social figures effectively aroused public awareness. Recently, they established tuberculosis clinics and published anti-tuberculosis publications, showing great effort. Based on the proposed three-year anti-tuberculosis plan, we hope it will be realized.

The importance of leprosy prevention in public health is well known. Over the past year, the Shanghai Leprosy Association has offered rewards for articles, attracting medical students' attention, which is worth noting. Efforts such as those of the Shanghai Children's Welfare Association and the establishment of children's dental hospitals by the Home Industries Cooperative can supplement the efforts of health authorities in public health. We hope that more public health associations will flourish in the future.

During the summer, the Shanghai Municipal Health Authorities diligently worked to prevent diseases among citizens, such as administering preventive injections, inspecting drinking water, handling waste, and killing stray dogs. As a result, infectious diseases such as cholera and smallpox were rare in the 23rd year of the Republic! This shows the value of preventive medicine. Not only that, Nanjing, Hankou, Beijing, and other places have also focused on disease prevention without negligence. In the past year, few vicious infectious diseases have spread within China, except for typhoid fever and dysentery. Therefore, all Chinese people should recognize the importance of preventive medicine.

There is another new and groundbreaking initiative: the Shanghai Anti-Tuberculosis Association, the Children's Welfare Association, the Children's Morning Post, the Municipal Education Bureau, the Municipal Health Bureau, and other five organizations jointly established a children's health camp at the middle school department of Tongji University in Wusong during the summer of the 23rd year of the Republic, with a semi-official character. Although the time was only six weeks, the results were unexpected. Most of the children who entered the camp were able to fulfill our ideal goals: developing good hygiene habits and improving their physical and mental health. Resting our hopes on the future of the nation with this camp is truly promising.

In the impending crisis of future wars, the authorities are aware of the importance of air defense and have conducted air defense exercises in Shanghai and Nanjing, which seem quite realistic. Major hospitals and the Red Cross in the area have designed simulated rescue plans, and it is expected that major cities will follow suit in the future.

Over the past year, the New Life Movement has gained momentum. The authorities have shown great determination to address the opium problem with a thunderous force, executing opium dealers and arresting opium smokers in various places in Nanjing and other places, mandating the strict prohibition of opium, which has had a significant and positive impact on public health. The strict inspections of public prostitutes and suppression of secret prostitutes in Beijing are also good deeds to improve national health. We sincerely hope that these efforts will continue.

After the recovery of the bandit areas in southern Jiangxi, the Shanghai Local Association commissioned Mr. Pang Jingzhou to take charge of disaster relief. Popular obstetrics hospitals were established in Hebei, Henan, Shanghai, Nanjing, and other places to provide free childbirth services to alleviate the suffering of poor mothers and children. In this year, these public health facilities were all things that we heard and were so happy that we could not sleep.

(13) Conclusion

The medical and health situation in our country in the past year has been roughly as described above. Although there may be omissions of certain facts, the general outline has been presented. Concluding this article, our impression is that Chinese medicine and health in the 23rd year of the Republic face: the lurking danger of medical education deviating from its purpose, frequent medical disputes, intense infighting among medical groups, the lingering boundaries of medical schools, traditional doctors still lost in dreams, public health failing to be popularized, the medical publishing industry barren and awaiting cultivation, and the new pharmaceutical industry only in its nascent stages. Therefore, where do we go from here? Please recognize the truth, make the greatest efforts in the 24th year of the Republic, reverse the critical situation, determine the goal, and work together! (The End)

Common Sense Q&A About Diseases 265

— Cheng Hanzhang

(52) Tropical Splenomegaly (Commonly Known as Black Fever)

(Q) What is tropical splenomegaly?

(A) It is a chronic feverish infectious disease that is endemic to certain regions, characterized by a very large spleen and liver, as well as anemia, wasting, and edema. It has been spreading rapidly in the Jiangbei area recently.

(Q) Why is it often referred to as black fever in the newspapers?

(A) This name is translated from the English "Black Fever." Because Westerners commonly call this disease "Black Fever." At the same time, they also call another infectious disease with a different cause, Rocky Mountain spotted fever, "Black Fever." Therefore, this name is fundamentally a mistaken common name from abroad (not everything from abroad is necessarily correct), and we do not need to imitate it.

(Q) What is the correct Western name for this tropical splenomegaly, and are there any other names?

(A) In Latin, it is Splenomegalia Tropica. In German, it is Tropische Splenomegalie. In English, it is Tropical Splenomegaly. There is also another name called "Kala Azar."

(Q) What is the pathogen of this disease?

(A) It is a type of flagellate, named Leishmania Donovani in honor of its discoverers, Leishman and Donovan.

(Q) Where does this pathogen parasitize in the patient's body?

(A) It parasitizes in the internal organs, especially in the spleen, bone marrow, and liver. It primarily parasitizes in endothelial cells.

(Q) Is there a relationship between the age of the patient and tropical splenomegaly?

(A) Most patients with this disease are young people.

(Q) How is the pathogen spread?

(A) As far as we know, the pathogen of this disease is transmitted from dogs to humans by the bites of several types of mosquitoes called Phlebotomus argentipes and Anopheles punctipennis, and a type of bedbug called Cimes hemipterus. There are often cases where multiple members of a family are infected.

(Q) What are the symptoms of tropical splenomegaly?

(A) At the onset of the disease, there are several weeks of continuous fever, and this type of fever often has large daily fluctuations (this is the first stage). In addition, it is accompanied by symptoms similar to dysentery, enlargement of the liver and spleen, and severe anemia. After two or three weeks of such fever and various symptoms, they disappear, but the enlargement of the spleen and liver continues, and the anemia gradually worsens.

(Q) Does this fever and remission repeat endlessly?

(A) Yes. The non-feverish periods of repeated fever and remission gradually shorten. After several months, the spleen gradually enlarges to a very large extent, extending into the lesser pelvis (second stage). At this time, the degree of anemia is even greater, and it progresses to the point of causing general cachexia and emaciation.

(Q) What are the symptoms in the third stage?

(A) The disease reaches its extreme in the third stage. The abdomen is very distended, and the skin takes on a dull, earthy color, hence the common name "black fever."

(Q) How long does the entire course of black fever take, and what is the outcome?

(A) The entire course of this disease takes six months to three years. The outcome is death due to cachexia and other complications (such as pneumonia, pulmonary tuberculosis, septicemia, etc.).

(Q) What is the treatment for this disease?

(A) Antimony preparations, such as tartar emetic, Neostibosan, or Neostam, are now used for intravenous injection, which is quite effective. Inject 0.1 grams per 100 pounds of body weight, made into a 4% solution, every other day. The total injection amount is approximately 3 grams.

Basic Knowledge of Ear, Nose, Throat, and Eye Hygiene 266

— Tang Renjin

(33) Scarlet Fever (Continued)

Because the rash resembles a sheet of red, the disease is also known as "Dan Sha". The rash usually first appears below the collarbone and on the neck, gradually (in about 24 hours) spreading to the face (less so), head, torso, and limbs. However, the area around the mouth and nose remains pale and does not develop a rash. This unique characteristic is of significant value in diagnosing scarlet fever. Sometimes, the rash can appear in different forms, leading to names such as papular, miliary, vesicular, pemphigoid, mottled, and hemorrhagic scarlet fever, based on its specific appearance. Hemorrhagic scarlet fever is usually severe and can be life-threatening. Fortunately, these atypical forms of scarlet fever are not very common in clinical practice.

Symptoms of the Throat in Scarlet Fever | The mucous membrane of the throat and tonsils become significantly red and swollen, known as scarlet fever tonsillitis. If the inflammation worsens, the soft palate and uvula also swell. At the same time, gray-white, greenish, or brownish coatings appear on the tonsils. The patient's suffering intensifies, and swallowing becomes increasingly difficult. These symptoms closely resemble pharyngeal diphtheria.

Changes in the Tongue Coating in this Disease | Are also quite distinctive and worth noting. Initially, there is a grayish-white or white coating on the tongue, but it soon gradually peels off, and the surface of the tongue becomes clean and bright red. The fungiform papillae also swell, making the tongue surface uneven and resembling the surface of a cat's tongue, hence the term "cat tongue." However, the "cat tongue" is rarely found in recent epidemics of scarlet fever.

Desquamation of Scarlet Fever | From the third or fourth day after the rash appears, the rash gradually fades. The areas where the rash appeared first also fade first. After about a week, the skin returns to its normal color, and the body temperature gradually decreases to normal. At this time, desquamation usually begins, following the same pattern as the rash, starting from the neck and gradually spreading to the torso and limbs. The desquamation can be like bran or in membrane-like sheets, hence the clinical terms "pityriasiform desquamation" and "membranous desquamation." (To be continued)

Etiological Treatment and Prevention of Pyorrhea Alveolaris (3) 268

— Lin Jianxian

| Treatment for Type C Pyorrhea Alveolaris |

This type of pyorrhea is caused by systemic diseases. Therefore, the primary treatment strategy is to eliminate the underlying cause. In this case, dentists must collaborate with general physicians to achieve effective results. The treatment is divided into systemic and local approaches. Local treatments, including surgical procedures and medications, are the same as those for Types A and B. Systemic treatment should be handled by general physicians. For pyorrhea caused by diabetes, the oral symptoms are very obvious, making diagnosis easier. However, the initial symptoms may not be apparent, so urine tests are crucial for dental diagnosis.

| Prevention of Pyorrhea Alveolaris |

The main cause of pyorrhea is the accumulation of calculus around the teeth. Therefore, removing calculus and maintaining oral hygiene eliminates the chance of developing the disease. Here are a few points:

(1) Visit a dentist every six months for an oral examination and professional teeth cleaning to completely remove calculus. This also allows for a detailed examination of the oral condition. The cost is minimal, and the benefits are significant.

(2) Brush your teeth regularly, three times a day. Use toothpaste or tooth powder containing antiseptics and astringents. Also, massage the gums with a toothbrush to strengthen and cleanse them. This method is effective in preventing gingivitis and pyorrhea because the medications can directly contact the gums and mucous membranes and penetrate the spaces around the teeth to exert their effects.

(3) If you notice gingivitis, red and swollen gums, soreness, or bleeding, which may indicate the onset of pyorrhea, consult a dentist immediately. At the same time, use the toothpaste mentioned above to brush your teeth and massage your gums to keep the mouth clean and promote early resolution of the inflammation.

(4) Pay attention to hygiene in daily diet and lifestyle. Avoid excessive indulgence and overwork. Also, get plenty of fresh air, sunlight, and appropriate exercise.

(5) If you discover any systemic diseases, consult a general physician immediately to prevent them from affecting your teeth.

The above five preventative measures are very effective for preventing pyorrhea. Early attention can prevent future problems. This article only covers simple and effective methods. Specialized surgical procedures that are too complex and difficult for the average reader to understand are omitted. (End)

A Brief Discussion on Pulmonary Tuberculosis (3)(10)(9) 269

— Hu Jiayan

What is the real value of X-rays in the diagnosis of this disease? We certainly cannot say that it is definitive for everything, nor can we say that all other examination methods can be eliminated after the application of X-rays. However, in ordinary clinical examinations, X-ray examinations often provide final corrections and supplements. The size, density, and shape of lesions, as described above, are excellent examples, as are the size and shape of cavities. As for lesions far from the surface of the lung, so-called central tuberculosis, physical examinations yield almost no information, even for extensive lesions. However, X-ray examination can completely reveal them, leaving no escape. As for differentiating between different types of the disease—exudative, proliferative, and cirrhotic—this can be difficult even in pathological anatomy! X-ray examination cannot completely take over this task, but the images of cirrhotic lesions are especially clearly defined, and the images of calcified lesions are especially dense. These are completely different from the images of exudative lesions. Regarding early diagnosis, the recognition of early lesions, X-ray examinations do not yield impressive results. If pathological anatomy yields 90%, then X-rays yield only about 10%. This gap is obviously too large, but it is limited by the facts. Readers should understand that the lungs are three-dimensional organs, and X-ray examination produces only a two-dimensional image. Lesions occurring in these many planes are all superimposed on a single plane. We cannot expect to make definitive judgments based solely on the image! In addition, for several model types of the disease, such as hilar and pulmonary vascular tuberculosis, apical tuberculosis, caseous pneumonia, and acute miliary tuberculosis, X-rays often reveal findings that supplement other examinations. However, these are all too specialized, and ordinary people do not need to know them in such detail, so they are all omitted here!

Regarding X-ray examinations, they usually involve both "fluoroscopy" and "photography." Most patients consider these to be redundant and meaningless. In fact, they each have their strengths and weaknesses, and neither should be abandoned. Photography allows for long-term preservation for continuous research, unlike fluoroscopy, which is a fleeting examination that leaves no record. However, fluoroscopy also has its unique advantages. For example, the movement of the diaphragm and ribs during breathing, the expansion and contraction of the lungs, the changes in the apex of the lung during coughing, and the pulsation of the heart and major blood vessels can only be clearly observed with fluoroscopy. Photography cannot achieve this.

The value of X-ray examination in the diagnosis of this disease has been outlined above! In summary, it often provides supplements and corrections to other clinical examinations and is worthy of praise. However, it does not contribute much to differentiating between types of the disease or determining whether lesions are rapidly progressing. This conclusion may disappoint some people. However, even from this point of view, its contribution to the benefit of humanity is beyond the description of this humble pen! (End of Chapter 8)

Free Talk

Three Years Ago Today 270

— Xicun

Three years ago today, in the first half of the day, I was in Wusong. I still remember getting up early in the morning and, as usual, taking a walk along the Huangpu River, looking out at the misty sea in the distance.

I opened a book and read a few lines, but I put it down. No, I was completely unable to concentrate on reading. The sound of the guns of Japanese imperialism on September 18th shattered my interest in reading. In the past, I used to come to the river every morning to read for an hour, but after that, I failed nine times out of ten. Looking at the scenery of the distant sea, I often thought of my hometown in the Northeast and worried about the devastation and pain my hometown was suffering. I was not someone who believed in "studying without forgetting to save the country." In fact, at that time, I neither wanted to save the country nor wanted to study. What bothered me day and night was an unspeakable feeling of depression and indignation!

After lunch, I planned to go for another walk by the river. Just as I was about to leave, Han Zhang ran up to me and said:

"Let's go! Let's go to Shanghai for a meeting! A fellow townsmen's association meeting. Let's go!"

I shook my head, but he dragged me away. As he walked, he muttered:

"You bookworm, the country is in trouble. Why aren't you rising up to save the country! You have to participate!"

Listening to him, it seemed that holding a fellow townsmen's association could save the country. Although I didn't want to save the country, I was very happy to hear that others could save the country and wanted to save the country. Especially we Northeasterners, we should save the country even more.

If holding a fellow townsmen's association could save the country and our homes, then I had to participate no matter what.

In the afternoon, we took a free train to Shanghai.

So, in the afternoon of today three years ago, I was in Shanghai.

The fellow townsmen's association meeting at the Zhongshe ended at half past six. The temporary curfew announced by the authorities of the concession blocked the residents' journey back to Wusong. At the same time, I heard others say that the Shanghai-Wusong trains had stopped running for the night, so even if I ran to the North Station, I might not be able to get back. I followed some fellow townsmen to the home of a fellow townsman living on Beler Road to stay overnight.

This fellow townsman lived in a small front room on the second floor. Adding so many people caused a great panic regarding sleeping arrangements. Not only were there not enough beds, but there were also not enough quilts. It was January 28th, still in the winter season, and it was difficult to sleep without a quilt at night. What to do? Everyone was a little anxious.

After a moment of hesitation, the homeowner came up with a solution. He didn't say it out loud. He first ran downstairs to the sub-landlord, and then when he came back up, we all understood. He was holding a box of mahjong tiles in his hand. Everyone laughed, and the problem was solved.

Almost everyone wants to play mahjong when they see it. Even in a national crisis, this pastime cannot be stopped. There were many of us, so we decided to draw lots. I lost, but I did have a place to sleep. I went to sleep at around ten o'clock. I remember telling the four warriors before going to sleep:

"Call me early tomorrow morning. I want to go back to Wusong early."

As I was sleeping, the people playing cards woke me up. I thought it was dawn, but the electric lights were still on. At the same time, I heard the voices of people in the front and back of the house.

"Get up quickly! It's started! The Japanese soldiers must have started fighting!"

After saying this, the person who woke me up left me and ran to the sundeck. Only I was left in the room, accompanied by the messy mahjong on the table.

It was midnight. I put on my clothes and went to the sundeck. A red glow rose to meet me. The sound of gunfire rang out like a string of pearls.

"So this is the start of the fighting."

"Good, this time we can vent our anger. The Japanese are too bullying!"

"That's right!"

"There must be a big fire, otherwise it wouldn't be so red."

"Probably in the Baoshan Road area, near the North Station?"

On the sundeck, in the alleyway, people were talking and staring at the same place in a daze. I thought, this time the war probably wasn't started by China, right? Of course not.

The second September 18th tragedy had begun again in Shanghai. The Japanese soldiers were so barbaric? I thought, this is probably what makes imperialism more civilized than our small and weak nation?

Today, three years later, has arrived again, reminding me of that day three years ago and prompting me to write this short memoir.

Where to Begin? 271

— Xiang Yu

If it weren't excessive, I would have to say a few words on such an important historical day. But where to begin has become the problem. The scope is too broad, and the problem is too serious. If we are not completely indifferent, we will naturally feel endless sadness for the ruined walls and crumbling buildings that are before our eyes, we will naturally feel endless sorrow for the lost territories, and we will naturally feel endless indignation for the traitors who are invading our territories and the enemy cavalry commanding them. Moonless Moonlit Night 272

— Xin Er

Everyone has probably heard of the scenery along the coasts and lakes of Southern Europe, such as Italy, which is mostly so beautiful and clear! But it seems that few have heard of a place in our China that, even at night, when there is no moon, still resembles a moonlit night scattered with beautiful, clear, silvery light.

This is the southwest that you think of whenever you mention the north! That remote border area of Dali, Yunnan, is the place where the world-famous marble is produced. No wonder the scenery and colors are so elegant. But who still worries about these lovely mountains and rivers—Dali!

On one side, it faces the sea, and on the other, it leans against Cangshan Mountain. In the middle of this embrace of sea and mountains is Dali, a hundred li of flat land—even better than the poor land of Sichuan. From beginning to end, it is all the same fields and houses, with the blue sky above, the clear blue sea, and the lush green mountains. The terrain of Dali is like a fish, a hundred li long and ten to twenty li wide. The entrances at the head and tail are where the sea and mountains meet.

Here, thanks to the abundance of natural products and the lack of capitalist economic devastation, the countryside, combined with such quiet and beautiful scenery, still seems to be lying leisurely.

At night, if you climb a high mountain and look out, almost all of Dali can be seen faintly. Within twenty or thirty li, even a tree can be distinguished. Even a shout from twenty li away can be heard clearly. The clarity and invigorating nature of the air and the pure white color of the sky make it look like a moonlit night at the time of the full moon!

The clouds in the sky are scattered gloomily, and the moon has hidden its face. However, from Dali city and the surrounding countryside, you can look up and see the trees on Cangshan Mountain, each one clearly and quietly standing tall. The earth is shrouded in a silvery light. Guests who come to Dali from outside must stare and exclaim in surprise:

"What a beautiful moonlit night!..."

But, piercing through the surrounding white mist, you cannot find a full moon. This moonless moonlit night makes people wonder if they are dreaming!

Desolate, bright, fresh, and refreshing, this night in Dali! It is as if it is not of this world! The atmosphere is so quiet and bright.

Arriving in Dali on this moonless moonlit night makes one feel as if they have stepped into a paradise, and their mind and spirit are lightened ten thousand times. This should be a mountain and river to be intoxicated with, a place to be reluctant to leave!

However, who can always remember Dali, which seems to be dreaming a beautiful dream? Who can visit it more often?

The Bai Li Erhai Lake of green water, the Cangshan Mountain of green mountains embracing Dali, and the scenery of the moonless moonlit night.

When will I be able to see your beauty again?

What Should Essays on Natural Science Actually Be About? 273

— Chao Jian

I myself have never written a scientific essay, so it is quite arrogant of me to say that other people's scientific essays are almost all badly written. If someone asked: What should essays on natural science actually be about? This question would leave me speechless, because I myself have never planned this matter thoroughly.

Now, I will write down some of the things that come to my mind at the moment. As for the places that are not enough or wrong, I hope that some friends will come out to supplement or correct them.

First, essays on natural science should seem to point out the shortcomings of current natural science, especially the shortcomings in methodology; because neither deduction nor induction can refute the many accumulated empirical materials.

Second, they should point out the inappropriateness of past natural scientists refusing to adopt new methods; at the same time, they should also point out that they had already intentionally or unintentionally adopted a part of the new methods in practice.

Third, they should remind ordinary natural scientists to abandon the attitude of only caring about "nature" and not caring about "society"; because the development of natural science, its prosperity, and its temporary stagnation are all closely related to people's lives.

Fourth, progressive methods should be used to organize the materials obtained from experience in each discipline; at the same time, the inherent organization and process of these materials should be discovered. The law of motion should be used to replace the law of cause and effect. By doing so, the foundation of each discipline will be built on its own contradictions, so that all of its materials constitute an organic system.

Fifth, the various disciplines of natural science should be connected into a network organization; the shifts from one discipline to another should be discovered in themselves.

Sixth, the special manifestations of new methods in natural science should be pointed out; at the same time, the general manifestations of new methods in thinking and social science should be pointed out.

Seventh, the achievements obtained by the above methods should be used to enrich the content of philosophy. On the one hand, they will make those distorted theories lose their last refuge.

Eighth, when you and I are shouting about saving the country, some people are also shouting the slogan of "saving the country through science and engineering." In recent publications, some people are also talking a lot about "science and engineering." We should point out which station current natural science has reached; how should we "catch up" to be called that; how should we not "chase the butt." And to point out how much relationship there is between science and engineering and saving the country.

Ninth, we should conduct a review of domestic publications such as "Science," "Science Quarterly," and "Scientific China" published in recent years. In this venue, we should also remind some people in the past that it is inappropriate to "only care about society and not nature."

Of course, many of the above questions can only be regarded as a goal at present, and cannot be implemented immediately. The question of "science and engineering" for "saving the country," the question of the old natural science taking the position of the "new" philosophy, have already been placed in front of us waiting for us to study, haven't they?

Little Ox and A-Fu 274

— Qin Wen

After two consecutive days of northwest winds, this morning when I woke up, the red sunlight was shining on the glass windows; the wind no longer howled, and the sky was clear, but it was cold. I happened to go to the window to look out and saw that the bottom of the small river was already visible. I remembered that yesterday evening, the river was still full, which I found a bit strange. Looking ahead, the large pond connected to the small river was also empty. It turned out that the sluice gate had been opened, draining the water, and many people were catching fish.

I could vaguely see fish flashing brightly on the raised nets. To get a clearer view, I washed my face and went over there.

The school foreman, Changsheng, was already standing there before me, asking a thin, tall man, "Little Ox, how many fish have you caught?"

"Only two or three," Little Ox replied, looking up, his bronze-colored face splattered with mud. He put in a lot of effort, taking a step, then throwing himself down to feel around with both hands. Then he took another step and repeated the same action.

"A-Fu! Are you here to catch fish too?"

Hearing Changsheng's question, I turned my head and saw a smiling young man, a newcomer.

"I'm here to catch fish. Do you want some?"

A-Fu replied like this while slowly rolling up his trousers; he lit a cigarette, biting it in his mouth, before slowly stepping into the pond.

Once in the middle of the pond, A-Fu just stood in a pool of water, quietly waiting. When he saw ripples on the surface, he quickly reached down, immediately grabbing a white fish, which he stuffed into the basket on his back as it flailed its tail.

The preparatory bell rang loudly. I had a class, so I hurried back to school. After the first class, I had congee for breakfast. I had no classes for the second and third periods, so I strolled back to the pond to watch them catch fish again. A-Fu was nowhere to be seen, but Little Ox was still taking a step, throwing himself down to feel around with both hands; then he took another step and repeated the same action.

His trouser legs were covered in mud, and there was no skin visible on his arms, as if they were two sections of muddy lotus root. Occasionally, he straightened up to stretch his back. Oh! His face was revealed, now covered with large black speckles. But he immediately bent down again,

still taking a step, throwing himself down to feel around with both hands; then taking another step and repeating the same action.

In the evening, Changsheng brought me dinner. After setting out the food basket, he smiled at me and then asked, "Mr. Xu! Do you want to eat fish? If you want some, I can bring it to you!"

"Did you catch fish too?" I asked.

"No," he replied, "Little Ox gave it to me. Speaking of which—Mr. Xu! Let me tell you; Little Ox and A-Fu both went to catch fish today, as you saw this morning. Little Ox worked harder and caught more. A-Fu arrived after Little Ox had been catching fish for a while. Little Ox was among the first to go. A-Fu only fished for an hour before leaving, while Little Ox was the last to leave. Naturally, Little Ox caught a bit more fish, maybe about half as much again. Actually, A-Fu caught fish faster, about four or five catties in an hour. Little Ox, in four or five hours, only caught about seven or eight catties in total. But A-Fu made more money; he rushed to sell his fish first, getting 24 cents a catty, and sold out quickly. When Little Ox carried his to sell, he could only get 16 cents a catty, and nobody wanted to buy it because they had already bought fish; also, it was late, and people were already eating lunch. Later, he could only sell it for 10 cents a catty, and still couldn't sell it all. He had no choice but to give it away, and he gave me one!"

Having said this, Changsheng stared at me, looking rather melancholic. I said that my stomach hadn't been feeling well lately and I couldn't eat fish, so he reluctantly walked away.

People are inherently either clever or not; not clever is called foolish. If there were no foolish people, there would be no such thing as cleverness.

The Human World (10) (1) 275

— Li Huiying

"No! No! You can't open today without me!"

"Then can you wait until twelve o'clock? We can't take customers until after ten, maybe it will be about right then."

She stepped back again, pleading.

"No! No!"

The Korean wanted the money; he had to get the money no matter what.

He was truly unreasonable, simply not letting anyone speak. But why was he being so unfriendly? Even if she owed him money, surely he could wait a few hours.

He retorted even more angrily:

"Other money can wait, but this money can't be paid on time!"

Now, it became even clearer to me that he was exercising his authority in the opium den business, which was why he could be so unreasonable. He was indeed the master of the opium den. The madam answered him meekly, like a mouse in front of an old cat, not daring to utter a single sound.

Finding no other way and unable to plead any further, the madam took off a gold ring from her own hand and another from Xiaoju's hand, placing them in Mr. Jin's hands, still saying with a smile:

"Then, Mr. Jin, would you please be so kind as to sell these for us?"

Who says their lives are easy? They are truly pitiful; they are slaves of slaves! Yes, my trip was not in vain; thanks to the guidance of my friend, I finally opened my mind to the ways of the world.

Xiaoju stood there blankly; my friend remained silent, but his flushed face and heavy breathing clearly showed that he was angry with this stranger. What was he angry about? Disrupting his good time? As for me, I felt that if people are born into this world and are unwilling to strive for progress, wanting only to live a life of complacent ease, they will be trampled upon by others for eternity!

What was unfolding before me was a perfect example.

The madam took this opportunity to explain the situation, as if afraid we wouldn't understand. She said that this was the monthly fee that had to be paid, and she didn't blame Mr. Jin for being angry, only herself for not having enough money beforehand. Then she smiled and asked Mr. Jin not to take it to heart. Mr. Jin didn't reply, tucked the rings into his pocket, and strode out without greeting anyone.

"Let's go too."

With that, my friend and I said goodbye to them and walked back onto the dark path. I instinctively felt that my feet were walking in another world, but no, I still hadn't escaped the human world, hadn't slipped out of this Harbin human world.

I have opened my mind to the ways of the world. I have definitely opened my mind to the ways of the world. (The End)
